After Liu communicated with Lin, Lin believed that the National Products Promotion and Disaster Relief Conference was very important, so he agreed to write to Kuang to allow the National Products Promotion and Disaster Relief Conference to be held first. His original letter stated: "Dear Mr. Zhongmou, This is to inform you that the Shanghai National Products Promotion and Disaster Relief Conference is jointly initiated by the China National Products Manufacturers Association, the Jiaxu Zhejiang Disaster Relief Association, etc. (omitted) It both utilizes national products and helps disaster victims, which is a win-win situation. The conference previously used the site opposite the Great World on Aidao Road as the venue. Now, because the owner of the land has gone to another place, there is no way to contact him. Thinking of your Penglai Market's vacant land, which is very suitable for holding national product business, I specially write this letter of introduction, and I hope that you will allow the loan to benefit the victims and help the righteous cause. Regarding the matter of Jiang Gufang of the National Products Business Publishing House borrowing the Penglai Market, which I introduced earlier, please temporarily suspend it. I am here to inform you. I wish you peace. Your younger brother, Lin Kanghou, February 21st."

Unprecedented Heavy Fog in the City Yesterday

Traffic Obstructed, Street Lights Lit for Travel

Ships Delayed, Imports and Exports Out of Schedule

Starting from 3:30 PM yesterday, the city was suddenly enveloped in an unprecedented heavy fog. Vehicles traveling on the roads had to light their headlights to proceed. Ship arrivals and departures were delayed, and aircraft were also affected. Details are as follows:

Traffic Obstructed

The weather in the city has been extremely stifling in recent days. The night before last, spring rain began to fall lightly, and yesterday morning was also filled with overcast skies and rain. Starting at 3:30 PM, a light fog suddenly appeared, and by 4:00 PM it gradually intensified. After 4:30 PM, an even heavier fog enveloped the city, obstructing traffic on the roads. Vehicles had to travel slowly, and only after the streetlights on both sides of the road were lit could vehicles move forward slowly. By evening, it became even thicker. One could not distinguish people dozens of feet away, as if one were in a vast ocean.

Ships Delayed

The ships that were unable to enter the port yesterday due to the fog included the Changsha from the Yangtze River under Taikoo, the Hesheng from Hong Kong under Jardine Matheson, and the Haiyan from Wenzhou under China Merchants. Exports included the Jihe (Yangtze) under Jardine Matheson and the Ningxing (Ningbo route) under Sanbei Company. As for the ships scheduled to depart today, such as the Xin Ningxing under Daxing, the Xin Ningxing under Ningshao, the Xin Beijing, Shashi, Huangpu, Shuntian, Sichuan, Xin Ning under Taikoo, the Jiangjing under China Merchants, the Pinghe, Hesheng, Fusheng, etc. under Jardine Matheson, they will only be able to depart on schedule after the weather clears up. Otherwise, they will have to be delayed. Other foreign ships, such as the Kasashimaru from Japan and a cargo ship from the Black Sea under a certain company, were also unable to enter the port.

Manager of Heshun Coal Briquette Factory Assassinated

Zhang Died

Four Suspects

Yesterday morning at [time unclear], [address unclear], Zhang, manager of [factory name unclear] Coal Briquette Factory was assassinated. Police investigation below.

Joint Coal Briquette Production

The Sihe Coal Briquette Factory, located in a shed at the above address, was founded by Ming Gui (60 years old) from Hebei, Xue Yushan, Wang Debao, and Xue Heshu from Qingjiang. Initially, the capital was only 450 yuan, but the business has grown steadily over the years. After eight years, the capital has increased to more than 1,700 yuan. Zhang served as the manager. Because the business scope was very small, Zhang also had to supervise the manufacturing and delivery, etc.

Sudden Assassination

Zhang's family also lived in Shanghai, but they all returned to their hometown at the end of last year due to matters in the countryside. Therefore, Zhang lived in the factory. At 0:30 AM yesterday, while Zhang was sleeping soundly, two men suddenly broke into the door, each holding a sharp dagger, and went straight into Zhang's bedroom. Without saying a word, they jumped up and dragged Zhang off the bed, stabbing his head and abdomen twice. Zhang woke up in extreme pain and fell to the ground, shouting "Ah ya!" Song Baiyan, a worker who shared a room with Zhang, woke up in shock and saw two figures running away in the darkness.

Rounding up the Murderers

Workers Song Baiyan and Chen San checked with a lamp and saw that Zhang had fallen in a pool of blood, on the verge of death. They immediately reported to the Robertson Road Police Station. Inspector Gu and Detective Team Leader Geng Shoubao, along with team leaders Cao Chuqiao and Zhang Desheng, received the report and immediately rushed to round up the murderers, who had already escaped without a trace. They sent the injured Zhang Minggui to the Red Cross Hospital for treatment. However, due to a two-inch-deep stab wound to the head and a three-inch-deep stab wound to the abdomen, the injuries were too severe, and he died shortly after arriving at the hospital without receiving treatment. Afterwards, two daggers, about five inches long and extremely sharp, were found in his room. They were taken back to the Caojiadu Branch Bureau.

Suspects Apprehended

Subsequently, according to the factory shareholder Xue Yushan and the deceased's nephew Zhang Yi, who reported to the bureau, the deceased Zhang Minggui was very kind and had never had any grievances with anyone. The only possible reason for the murder was that Fan Weicai, He Anyi, and four other workers hired by the factory last winter were suspended by Zhang for violating factory rules. Fan and others hated Zhang very much, so Fan and others were suspected. After receiving the report, Wang Bicheng immediately ordered detectives Wang Yixin, Shi Yulin, Xu Deming, and Du Jingxiang to go to the Putuo Road Police Station and, together with the detectives dispatched, to the back shed in Beida Xuli, Robertson Road, to arrest Fan and He and take them into custody at the police station for temporary detention, pending a written report for questioning today. Chief Wang Dasui ordered Inspector Gu and the detective team to quickly apprehend the murderers and bring them to justice, as the case involved a murder.

Zhang Pengchun Discusses Chinese Drama from Three Perspectives

——The Following are the Directions for Future Efforts——

(1) Should have Analysis and Recording

(2) Revise the Script and Performance

(3) Should have more New Creation

Dr. Zhang Pengchun, a professor at Nankai University, accompanied Mei Lanfang to Russia this time to assist in everything. Mr. Zhang has studied drama for a long time. Yesterday, he spoke with reporters about Chinese drama. According to Mr. Zhang, we can look at Chinese drama from three perspectives. The first is from a social status perspective, the second is from a theatrical art perspective, and the third is from a cultural change perspective. (1) From a social status perspective on Chinese drama, we have always looked down on Chinese drama, thinking that it is just a form of entertainment. Literati and scholars who are interested in drama, from the Yuan Dynasty to the recent twenty or thirty years, have only regarded scripts as a form of amusement. Drama in Europe has been comparatively [unclear word] more prosperous. From the Greek period to the modern era, although there were hundreds of years of seeming silence, drama had long been recognized as a legitimate branch of literature. Since Chinese drama has been looked down upon by the literati, its social status is also seemingly very low. Even now, I am afraid that we [unclear word] cannot avoid the old notion of looking down on Chinese [unclear word] and those who are related to drama. It is not [unclear word], but recently, because Western views on drama have gradually spread to China, everyone also knows that drama should be studied and created, and the social status of drama has also increased. (2) From a theatrical art perspective on Chinese drama, Chinese drama is different from Western drama. It is neither spoken drama nor opera. The organizational method of Chinese drama is different. In terms of writing, Chinese drama is a mixture of songs and recitations, and it is not entirely colloquial. For example, in the section of Si Lang Visiting His Mother in the Palace, the person playing Yang Yan Hui himself sings "Yang Yan Hui Sits in the Palace Courtyard..." There are very many such examples. The above is about the writing aspect of Chinese drama. Below, I will talk about the performance aspect. If we look at Chinese drama from the perspective of modern realism drama, it is easy to see Chinese drama as an incompletely evolved social legacy. However, the difference between Chinese drama and ordinary modern realism drama lies in the fundamental acknowledgment of the distance between "art" and "daily forms." For example, the singing and dialogue on stage are different from everyday language, the body movements on stage are different from everyday actions, the makeup on stage is different from everyday appearances, and the costumes on stage are different from everyday clothing, etc. In modern times, some people are dissatisfied with realistic art and want to create a form of art that breaks free from the bonds of daily forms. However, the methods of this general new art and the methods of Chinese drama have different points. They want to use personal divine sense to create a special way. Their creation naturally has a distance from daily forms, but it is difficult for others to understand. The method of Chinese art is based on handed-down customs and gradually forms an artistic "alphabet." For example, various body movements can all be analyzed into many simple movements. These simple movements are the "letters" of the body movements. Because these "letters" are handed down, they can be understood by the audience. Although the stage walk is different from ordinary walking, the audience can understand that the walking on stage should be like this. Therefore, Chinese drama, on the one hand, breaks free from the bonds of daily forms, and on the other hand, it can be understood by the audience. This is the difference between Chinese drama and modern realistic drama, and it is also the difference between Chinese drama and "drama that creates artistic forms individually." Since various forms are handed-down customs, how can we see personal strengths or personal creations? In general, it can be divided into three points: (1) A deep understanding and masterful use of each form. (2) The spirit of unity and integration of all forms. (3) After becoming proficient in the old forms, feeling the need to create new forms, and then creating them. If the new creation is accepted by colleagues and the audience, it is considered a teachable form. The reason why Chinese drama was well-received by drama researchers when it was performed in the United States last time was probably due to the above-mentioned characteristics of Chinese drama. Three years ago, when I went to the Soviet Union to visit education and drama, I had the opportunity to talk with the Soviet director Meyerhold about a method he used to train actors. He called this method "Bio-Mechanics." What he meant was to train actors in various movements so that emotions and body movements are closely linked. He said, "This method was produced by taking the method of training actors in Chinese drama as a reference." From this, it can be seen that Russian directors already have a considerable understanding of Chinese drama. (3) From a cultural change perspective on Chinese drama, the cultural methods of any country or era should be studied and preserved if they have noteworthy or valuable points of reference. However, we cannot say that this achievement can exist unchanged for a long time, because the cultural product of a place or a time must change with the "cultural climate." We should acknowledge that the scope of Chinese drama is narrow. Within this narrow scope, in order to enable Chinese drama to continue to exist in the world, we must strive in the following three directions: (1) Create systematic analyses and detailed records. Use tools such as photography, film, phonograph, text, and diagrams to make detailed analyses and systematic records of existing body movements, singing styles, dialogues, etc., for preservation and research. (2) Organize and revise scripts and performance methods. The plot must be deepened, the music must be accurately arranged, and the body movements must have a certain position and size. (3) Create new scripts, new music, new body movements, new makeup, and new scenery based on its own characteristics and using world art and science – non-realistic, stylized. If we do this, Chinese drama can occupy a considerable position in the modern world.

Request from the United Cement Industry Association to Rectify the Guangdong-Hankou Railway's Purchase of Foreign Cement

The United Cement Industry Association of China recently reported that the Zhushao section of the Guangdong-Hankou Railway Bureau had ordered 40,000 barrels of "Red Dragon" cement from Haiphong, Annam, French Indochina, and imported it duty-free. This, they argued, adversely affected the sales of domestic cement and the spirit of the government's efforts to prevent dumping and increase tariffs. Therefore, they recently petitioned the Executive Yuan and the Ministries of Railways, Communications, Finance, and Industry, requesting them to instruct the Railway Bureau to use domestic goods in the future and to promote domestic cement as much as possible to maintain the real economy. The original text of their petition to the Ministry of Finance is as follows: Request to the effect that the Guangdong-Hankou Railway Bureau's purchase of foreign cement and duty-free import has caused public concern, and earnestly requesting relief to prevent further losses. Cement is a vital material for all construction projects. There are currently five cement factories nationwide, with an annual output of over four million barrels, which is more than enough to meet the country's needs. In terms of quality, they all exceed the standards of European and American cement. In recent years, not only domestic merchants have been using domestic cement for construction, but also foreign-managed or controlled projects, such as the Shanghai Public Concession and French Concession's two municipal councils, have been happy to purchase Chinese products due to their reasonable prices and high quality. However, according to reports from member companies of the Association, "The Guangdong-Hankou Railway Bureau has abandoned domestic goods and purchased a large quantity of Red Dragon cement imported from French Annam, amounting to as many as 40,000 barrels. According to investigations, the quantities transported in batches are listed as follows:

(Explanation) The "Shun Kang" vessel transported directly from Haiphong to Hankou, while the rest were transshipped from Shanghai by Butterfield & Swire "Blue Funnel Line" ships, totaling 40,000 barrels.

The imported Red Dragon cement was exempted from import duties and consolidated taxes (approximately 4.20 yuan per barrel), so the bagged price for delivery in Hankou was approximately 5.23 yuan per barrel. It has been established that civil servants and government agencies should, as far as possible, use domestic goods for materials they use or purchase. This has long been a resolution of the Central Government and the Executive Yuan, and has been circulated for implementation. If the Guangdong-Hankou Railway's purchase of imported cement is based on quality, Red Dragon cement is not of superior quality. Compared to British cement standards, its performance may even be inferior to domestic products. In Shanghai construction projects, this brand of cement was previously only used for painting walls, which shows its quality. If it is based on price, the Railway Bureau did not follow the procurement principles and did not widely inquire about prices from domestic cement companies to make comparisons. Moreover, in the southern section of the Guangdong Railway, the locally produced Xicun Cement is nearby, and the price should not be too high. Furthermore, the obligations and responsibilities of domestic manufacturers to the country and society are incomparable to the indifference of foreign merchants. Even if the price of the same product is slightly different, the government should, from the perspective of the overall national economy, purchase domestic goods as much as possible to promote domestic industries. However, the Railway Bureau is not doing this, and is willing to purchase foreign goods, causing the country to increase its losses. How can the gains and losses be calculated? Considering both quality and price, there is no reason to use Red Dragon cement. Moreover, at a time when the trade deficit is increasing year by year and large amounts of silver are flowing out, and people from all walks of life are trying to remedy the situation, how can we tolerate domestic construction projects violating central government orders and economic principles by purchasing large quantities of foreign goods? How can the government show its initial intention to protect real industries and set an example for the people to happily use domestic goods? This is what the Association members are surprised and puzzled by regarding the Guangdong-Hankou Railway Bureau's purchase of Red Dragon cement. Furthermore, since the consolidated cement tax was increased from 6 jiao to 1.20 yuan per barrel, merchants were already worried about the increased burden. Fortunately, the government also increased import duties, so domestic cement was somewhat protected and the country's tax revenue increased. Now, if state-owned railways openly purchase foreign goods and create an example of duty-free imports, the tariff protection will become a mere formality, and domestic manufacturers will not be able to survive under this heavy tax. As a result, the country's tax revenue will also be affected. Moreover, the Association believes that foreign goods shipped to China are mostly of a dumping nature, and their selling prices in China are often reduced to below cost or below the selling prices in their countries of origin. Cement is particularly prone to dumping. Since the government increased import duties, the amount of imports has decreased. Last year, imported cement accounted for only about 50% of the amount in 1933. However, considering the production of various factories, it has not yet reached its maximum capacity. It is clear that this industry still needs the joint support of the government and society. If the Guangdong-Hankou Railway Bureau is allowed to import Red Dragon cement duty-free, it will remove the barriers and help promote dumping, which is not the government's original intention in revising the tariff regulations, and may be ridiculed by foreigners. The Association witnesses the domestic production industry declining day by day, and the national economy in a precarious state. If the somewhat successful cement industry is not urgently requested to be protected by the government, it is feared that a major disaster will occur in the future, leading to mutual destruction, and the society and national economy will inevitably be affected. The Association feels a sense of crisis and dares not remain silent. Therefore, we dare to lay out the facts and earnestly request your review and approval (instruct the Ministry of Railways) to order the Guangdong-Hankou Railway Bureau to use domestic cement for all future needs, and that your ministry should stop issuing duty-free licenses for imported cement in the future, and also issue a general order to its subordinates to purchase domestic cement as much as possible for construction projects to prevent losses and maintain the real economy, which would be in the public interest. Furthermore, the Association was reorganized from the former United Cement Factory of China, and has been reported to the Shanghai Special City Party Department for approval and registration, and is currently applying for registration. This is stated together. The person submitting the petition is the United Cement Industry Association of China.

Children's Day Painting Exhibition Held its First Preparatory Meeting Yesterday

Taking Wuben, Shangwen, and Xicheng Schools as Venues

Four Groups Established, with the Bureau of Education as the Head of Collection

To commemorate Children's Day, the Municipal Children's Happiness Association, the Chinese Art Education Society, and others have launched a children's painting exhibition. Yesterday afternoon at 2:00 PM, the first preparatory meeting was held at the Art Education Society in the Confucius Temple Park. More than ten people attended, including Hu Shuyi (representing Qian Fugong), Qian Fugong, Shi Chongpeng, Zhu Zhiwei, Lu Yunda, Zhou Wangyun, Shi Lianhuang, Shi Wenbin, Fu Boliang, and Zhang Meisun. (2) Discussion of the detailed rules for collection, which were approved. (3) Decision on the budget of the association, which was approved. (4) Decision on the scope of reference, which was approved. All entries from registered municipal or private primary schools, limited to one-tenth of the number of students. Individuals are also free to participate. (5) The Association will award prizes to excellent entries and publish the best ones in the Children's Morning News for encouragement, which was approved. (6) Decision on the venues: Senior level at Wuben, intermediate level at Shangwen, and primary level at Xicheng, to be delivered by 9:00 AM on April 3. (7) Decision on the exhibition dates: April 4 to April 6, for a total of three days. (8) Establishment of four groups: general affairs, collection, publicity, and review. The Bureau of Education was appointed as the head of general affairs, the Bureau of Education and the Art Education Society as the heads of collection, the Children's Morning News and the Children's Happiness Association as the heads of publicity, and the Art Education Society as the head of review. (9) It was decided that Hu Shuyi and Shi Chongpeng would apply to the Bureau of Education for funds, which was approved. (10) A request will be submitted to the Bureau of Education to issue a circular to all schools to participate, which was approved. (11) The collection of prizes will be handled by the Children's Happiness Association. (12) The appointment of judges was decided. Pan Gongzhan was appointed as the head judge, and Pan Tangguanzhi, Hu Shuyi, Jiang Danshu, Hu Minzhai, Yu Jifan, Feng Zikai, and Zhang Chunbo were appointed as judges. (13) The location of the office was decided, and it was decided to temporarily borrow the Bureau of Education's office for work.

Various Licenses for the Two Roads Will Be Issued Quarterly

Effective from April 1

Various licenses for vehicles, ships, hotels, stalls, and teahouses on the two roads have traditionally been issued monthly, which is a complicated procedure. To simplify matters, all types of licenses will now be issued quarterly each year, i.e., they will be renewed in January, April, July, and October each year. This measure will be implemented from April 1 of this year.

Hot Water Bottle Manufacturing Association Rectifies Market Prices

All Industries in the City Stop Business for One Day

Meeting to Discuss Increasing Market Prices

The Shanghai Hot Water Bottle Manufacturing Industry Association, in view of the fact that the city's commerce has been affected by the sluggish market for many years and surrounded by the dumping policies of foreign goods, resulting in frequent price drops and business declines, has now reached the point where factories are stopping work, going out of business, and going bankrupt. If this continues without rectification, the future will be unthinkable. The Association, learning from past mistakes and to maintain the original position of the emerging domestic industry, recently convened all industries in the city to discuss remedial measures. It was resolved that all industries in the city would stop business for one day on the 21st of this month and stop transporting goods to customers. On that day, all industries and factories were convened to discuss the issue of increasing market prices. The details of the meeting are listed below: (1) The meeting was held as scheduled, and Gan Dounan was elected as the chairman. The chairman first reported the purpose of the meeting and the resolutions of the previous session. (2) Regarding how to increase market prices for this year's opening, it was resolved that ordinary goods should be slightly increased according to the past selling prices of each factory, and colored goods should be increased by each factory at its discretion. (3) Regarding how to handle any violations or disruptions of the above price increase resolution, which was signed and approved by all industries, it was resolved that any factory (whether a member or not) that violates the above resolution should be reported to the higher authorities for strict punishment in accordance with industry regulations. (4) The date for the implementation of the price increase was decided, and it was resolved that it would be announced in the newspaper and strictly implemented from the 22nd of this month. (5) Regarding how to handle contracts previously signed between factories and customers, it was resolved that all contracts would be terminated and invalidated from the date of the announcement. If any disputes arise, they can be reported to the Association for assistance.

The Jinghu Railway Continues to Issue Fourth-Class Passenger Tickets Between Lingkou and Danyang

The Jinghu Railway originally planned to issue fourth-class passenger tickets between Lingkou and Danyang on a trial basis for six months, ending on January 30 of this year. Subsequently, it was found that the number of passengers between the two stations had increased significantly compared to the previous period. For the sake of caring for the common people, the aforementioned fourth-class passenger tickets will continue to be issued.

Bizarre Theft Case in the Diamond District

An Elegant Young Lady Whose Dress Does Not Resemble That of a Pickpocket

Taking Off Her Coat Revealed a Brooch That Could Not Possibly Be Pawned

Pang Zhenglong, a woman from Anhui, is in her early twenties and has a strong physique, resembling a great man. She once studied at the Anhui Higher Normal School and now resides at No. 15 Shude Lane, Yaozhu Jiao Road, French Concession. At 5:45 PM on the 28th of last month, the woman went alone to the Shanghai Old Goods Store at No. 598 Nanjing Road, stating that she wanted to buy a necklace. The shop assistant, seeing that she was dressed elegantly, considered her to be a young lady from a good family and immediately treated her attentively. He took out necklaces from the cabinet for her to choose from. The woman took off her black coat and placed it next to the cabinet, examining the necklace around her neck, touching it with her hand, and discussing the price. After a long time, she still found the price too high. She returned the necklace, took her coat, and left without a word. That evening, the store checked the items in the cabinet and discovered that a

diamond brooch

worth 220 yuan had disappeared. Since the woman had placed her coat next to the cabinet, they suspected that she might be responsible. They reported this to the Old Gate Police Station. Because they did not know the woman's whereabouts, they were unable to investigate. At about 5:00 PM the day before yesterday, the woman went to the Shanghai Old Hairpin Store again. Her clothes were even more glamorous, wearing a green woolen Western-style coat, a red Western-style skirt, yellow stockings, and yellow leather shoes, which attracted even more attention. The shop assistant saw her gracefully enter the store. Although old suspicions resurfaced, he had no evidence and could not ask her about it. He still treated her attentively. After the woman left, he immediately sent a friend to follow her, directly to No. 936 Xiafei Road, French Concession, to the

Hong Sheng Pawnshop

The woman entered the pawnshop and took out a pawn ticket from her bag. The pawnshop clerk thought she was redeeming an item. After examining the pawn ticket, he took out a diamond brooch. The woman claimed that she was not redeeming it, but wanted to increase the loan amount. The pawnshop clerk estimated that since it had been pawned for 150 yuan previously, he could only add 26 yuan. He asked the woman if she agreed. The woman nodded. At this time, the friend who had followed her from the Shanghai Old Goods Store had identified the brooch as the original item. He immediately used the telephone nearby to report to the Old Gate Police Station, which dispatched detective Wang Shanqing to rush to the pawnshop to arrest her. However, the woman had already disappeared like a yellow crane. Detective Wang then reported to the French Concession Police, who dispatched additional detectives to assist in the arrest. At 6:30 PM, they learned that the woman had returned to her residence after obtaining the loan amount,

accompanied by two young

men, and went to the Huifang Food Company at No. 206 Taisdelang Road to have a meal. They immediately followed and arrested them all and brought them back to the police station. After questioning by the police chief, one of the two men, Zhang Guanjin, and the other, Nong Minnan, both confessed to being university students. The loan amount pawned by the woman was also found on Zhang. The pawned brooch was also recovered. At that time, Pang confessed to stealing the jewelry and pawning it, and said that she and Zhang Nong were classmates and owed Zhang money, so she pawned the item to repay the debt and had no other relationship. The police chief then

released the two men

and sent the woman to jail. Yesterday morning, she was escorted to the First Special District Court, where Judge Zhan Liangce conducted the trial. Zhang Shizhu, the police lawyer, presented the case and requested that the defendant be punished for theft. Judge Zhan felt that the woman's appearance did not resemble that of a pickpocket, but now she had been caught with the stolen goods. According to the police lawyer, the woman had already confessed at the police station. After repeated and detailed questioning about the reasons for the theft, the woman explained the process of the theft and her remorse in detail. She said that her family was wealthy and her father was a member of the upper class and liked antiques and precious jewelry. The first time she passed by the Shanghai Old Goods Store, she went in to inspect because she saw that there were

necklaces for sale

However, because she did not have much money, she did not buy anything. When she returned to her residence, she took off her coat and saw that there was a brooch attached to the inside of the coat. She suddenly remembered that she had placed her coat on the jewelry box at the store. This pin might be from the box. She originally intended to return it immediately, but her close friend Wang Yufeng was ill and hospitalized in the Dahua Hospital and had repeatedly borrowed money for medical expenses, but she had been unable to respond because she had no money. Having obtained this brooch, she took it to the hospital to help people in need. She initially did not tell her friend where the pin came from, and Wang gladly accepted it and asked her to exchange it for cash. However, she was an educated woman and should not have committed this dishonorable act. After thinking about it, she felt

very sorry

and repeatedly wanted to go to the store to explain, but she did not have the courage, so she wanted to go but stopped. Yesterday, she went to the store again and originally intended to confess herself and ask the store to give her some time to raise money to repay it. Unexpectedly, after arriving, the people in the store were very attentive, so it was still difficult for her to speak. She returned in disappointment. On the way, she remembered that she owed Zhang Guanjin 40 yuan, and Zhang was leaving Shanghai today and had come to

demand payment

So she went to the pawnshop again to pawn the item for the money. She had already returned 20 yuan to Zhang. After confessing, she sobbed incessantly. Judge Zhan was lenient because the defendant was a first-time offender. After confessing, she sobbed incessantly. Judge Zhan was lenient because the defendant was a first-time offender and sentenced her to a fine of 50 yuan. The original stolen goods were returned to the owner, who was asked to quickly return them to the defendant. After Pang was fined, her male friend waited outside the courtroom. When he saw her come out, he immediately went forward to comfort her, and she was still crying bitterly. This is truly a rare case.

Page 12

Record of the Continued Trial of the Tang Jiapeng Assassination Case, Wang Xinggao

The Informant Zhao Guangfu Suddenly Changed His Testimony Again

Claiming That Wang Xinggao Had No Connection to This Case

Tang Jiapeng, a native of Ningbo and former manager of the Great World Amusement Park, also known as A Yu, was suddenly shot and assassinated in front of the Great World at about 1:00 AM on June 18, 1933, and died. At the same time, a pedestrian, Wu Guangcai from Yangzhou, was passing by and was killed by a stray bullet. Two months later, the French Police Special Agency arrested the criminals, Zhang Tinggui, a native of Funing, also known as Zhang Xiaosizi, and Zhao Guangfu, a native of Yangzhou. They were sent to the Second Special Court, which sentenced Zhang to 20 years in prison and Zhao to life imprisonment, both with permanent deprivation of civil rights. The case

was concluded after three trials and sent to prison for execution. Recently, the French Police, based on information from the arrested Zhao Guangfu, dispatched detectives to the Central Hotel on Wuma Road on the evening of December 13 of last year, together with the Old Concession Police, and arrested Wang Xinggao, a native of Funing, who was alleged to be the mastermind of the case. He was transferred to the Second Special Court and prosecuted for the crime of premeditated murder. During the interrogation, Wang stated that he had been working in the political arena and served as a warden in the First Prison of Hubei from August/September 1932 to August 1933. He denied participating in the murder of Tang Jiapeng, etc. After receiving instructions to postpone the investigation and re-interrogate him, the matter was reported in previous newspapers. After the Second Special Court transferred the case to the Hubei Higher Court for investigation, it was not until recently

that a reply was received. The trial judge, Tai Huicui, then scheduled a hearing for yesterday afternoon to summon the witnesses in the case for continued interrogation. At 2:30 PM, Judge Xiong, accompanied by Secretary Tao Zongkan, opened a special court in the Second Court. Lawyer Gu Shouxi represented the Police Affairs Office in court. Three lawyers, including Shen Xingxia and Zhang Qikai, who were hired by the defendant, arrived on time. Many relatives and friends of Wang, both male and female, attended the hearing, making the courtroom crowded and almost impossible to move. After the judge took the bench, he ordered the bailiff to bring the defendant, Wang Xinggao, to the front of the court. He said to Wang, "You said you were working in the First Prison of Hubei. Now, after an investigation by this court to the Hubei Higher Court, according to the reply from the Hubei Higher Court ordering the First Prison to respond, you were working there as an

extra staff member without a signing-in book. This evidence is very weak. Do you have any other strong evidence to present?" Wang replied, "I dare to say that I worked there because there was a signing-in book. Sometimes I signed in, sometimes I didn't. If the warden ordered me to go out to handle other matters, I would not sign in at the prison. If I worked in the prison, I would definitely sign in. I went to Wuchang in June 1932 and took over on August 1st or 2nd. I did not take my wife with me. In February 1933, I returned to Shanghai because my wife was pregnant. I asked for leave to return to Shanghai in August 1933." The judge asked, "You said you came back from Hubei. What evidence do you have?" Wang replied, "I

have a leave slip that can be checked." The judge asked, "You confessed at the police station that you were on vacation in June 1933 when Tang Jiapeng was murdered." Wang replied, "I was in Wuchang at that time. I came back in July." At this point, the court summoned witnesses Wang Zhou Shi (defendant's wife), Wang Chen Shi (defendant's concubine), Ma Baoting, Jiang Huanzhang, Ren Hepei, Cao Aliuyi, Xu Lianzhou, Xu Desheng (former Chief of the Inspection Office of the 26th Army in Zhabei), Qian Yumin (detective of the French Police), and others to court. After questioning each person about their age, address, and occupation, the judge said to each witness, "Today, you have been summoned to court to testify. Except for Zhou and Chen, who are husband and wife with Wang Xinggao and are not required to swear an oath, all witnesses must swear an oath and tell the truth. If you tell a lie, you will be prosecuted for

perjury when it is discovered in the future." Each person agreed and signed the oath, and then was ordered to leave the court and wait for questioning. The judge asked Wang again, "When did you go to work in the First Prison of Hubei?" Wang replied, "I went on June 30, 1932, and took over on August 1st or 2nd. My monthly salary was 16 yuan. On July 25, 1933, I applied for leave because my wife was giving birth and was approved on the 28th. I left that day and worked there for about a year. I never asked for leave before. I also did not go to Shanghai in January 1933." The judge asked, "The police sent detectives to your home to investigate and asked your wife, Zhou, who said that you came back to Shanghai in January and stayed for more than ten days." Wang replied, "No." The judge asked, "According to your confession, you were in Hubei in June 1933. Why did Zhao Guangfu confess that he was drinking tea with you at a teahouse on June 17?" Wang replied, "No, let him provide evidence. He

is slandering me. His other name is Zhao Debiao. In April 1928, he set fire to the Tongtai Pawnshop on Meiyuan Road in Zhabei for robbery. I couldn't catch him, so he bears a grudge and slanders me." The judge asked, "Zhao Guangfu confessed that on June 16, he and Zhou Ermujiang were drinking tea at the Renhe Teahouse, and you were also there. You introduced Sun Er to him and told him that you had a feud with the manager of the Great World and wanted him to kill him (referring to Tang), and promised to give him 100 yuan after the deed was done. Is this true?" Wang replied, "It's really a miscarriage of justice. There is absolutely no such thing." At this point, the court summoned witnesses for questioning. Wang Zhou Shi testified, "Wang Xinggao is my husband. After marrying Chen, he often lives at Chen's place and does not often come to my house. I know that he

went to Hubei in May 1932 and came back in September 1933. When the detective came to ask me, I did not say that my husband came back in January." Wang Chen Shi testified, "I married Wang Xinggao when I was 23 years old. He went to Hubei in May 1932 and came back in August 1933." Ma Baoting testified, "I run a stove shop on Hengfeng Road in Zhabei. I know Wang Xinggao. On August 1, 1933, I met Wang on Sima Road. He asked him and said he had just returned from Hubei. After talking a few words, he left." Ren Hepei testified, "I run a sand and gravel business. I met Wang at the Changle Teahouse. He said he had returned from Hubei." Xu Lianzhou testified, "I run a sand and gravel business." His words were the same as Ren's. Jiang Huanzhang testified, "I opened a

Renhe Teahouse on Hengfeng Road. I have never seen Wang Xinggao come to drink tea." Xu Desheng testified, "I was the Chief of the Inspection Office of the 26th Army in April 1927. Wang Xinggao was a captain in my office. I ordered Captain Wang to arrest Zhao Debiao for the Tongtai Pawnshop fire robbery case. Wang came to my house the day he returned from Hubei. Because I was sick, he left after saying a few words." The judge then ordered Zhao Guangfu to be brought to court. According to his testimony, "While I was in custody, I thought of Wang Jinkui in the Tang murder case, so I hated him for causing me to be wrongly accused. Later, someone said that Wang Jinkui had now changed his name to Wang Xinggao, so I had to investigate and reported it to the police. Now, I am speaking from my conscience. The Wang Xinggao in this case has no connection to the Tang murder case." The judge asked, "Then

why did you still identify him in court last time?" Zhao replied, "I used to have an affair with a Suzhou woman and rented a house to live together. Later, I heard that Wang had taken her and married her as his fourth concubine, so I hated him and accused him, using public office to avenge private revenge. I recognized him in court last time because I had been in custody for a long time and had not seen the light of day, so I was confused and made a mistake. I have known Wang since 1929, but I don't call him that." Zhang Tinggui, also known as Xiaosizi, was brought to court and testified, "I don't know Wang Xinggao. I have only heard of Wang Jinkui, but I don't know him." At this point, it was late. The court ordered the clerk to read the minutes and then ordered a postponement to March 6 in the afternoon for further interrogation of the witnesses in the case. The defendant was still remanded in custody. When the court adjourned, it was already six o'clock, and the lights of thousands of homes were lit.

The Sichuan-Kang Industrial Bank is the largest financial institution in Sichuan, with its head office on Datong Street in Chongqing and branches in major trading ports. Two Cases of Robbery

Aidotuo Road: At around 6 PM yesterday, at a residence with the address No. 4, 15th Lane, on Aidotuo Road, near Danshui Road, four bandits suddenly barged in. Three of them were armed with handguns, and one was unarmed. They first guarded the front and back doors, threatening and preventing anyone from making a sound, and assigned bandits to watch over the people. They then forced the residents to hand over the keys to chests and cabinets, proceeded to rob the place, overturning boxes and emptying baskets, searching everywhere thoroughly. After about half an hour, they left with their loot. Afterward, the victim tallied the losses, which amounted to over 500 taels of silver in cash, foreign currency, and jewelry. He immediately reported the incident to the police station in charge, requesting an investigation and pursuit of the criminals.

Guangxi Road: At a certain coal store located at No. 128 Guangxi Road, around 9 PM last night, just as they were preparing to close for the day, five robbers suddenly appeared. Only two of them were armed with handguns. After entering the store, they immediately shouted at everyone to stop and not move, and assigned one robber to guard them. They then ordered the owner to hand over the key to the cash box, opened the box, and stole all the cash and foreign currency inside, totaling 170 yuan. After obtaining the loot, the robbers fled. By the time the police arrived, the robbers were long gone. The owner then went to the police station in charge to report the incident, requesting an investigation and pursuit of the criminals.

Apprentice Climbs Over Roof to Report Crime

Three Robbers Arrested One After Another

The robbers Zhang Xuewen from Haizhou, Zhou Yushan from Qingjiang, and Gu Yinghan from Siyang, along with their gang, armed with weapons, went to Han Youjin's silk shop, a native of Yangzhou, located at No. 7 Tongle Lane, Huasheng Road, at 6:25 PM the day before yesterday. Zhang pulled out a gun, and aimed at Han, threatening and preventing him from making a sound, demanding that he hand over his valuables. Zhou and Gu retreated to keep watch. At that time, apprentices Yao Defu and Yao Changgen were quite alert and climbed from the balcony on the upper floor onto the roof, jumped down into the neighboring houses, and secretly went out to report to the Yulin Road police station and the reserve team. Immediately, Chinese and foreign detectives arrived and found the main gate locked. They entered through the back door, first arresting Zhang, seizing a handgun, and five bullets. Subsequently, Zhou and Gu were arrested nearby. All three were taken to the police station and detained. Yesterday morning, they were sent to the Third Criminal Court of the First Special District Court. The Shanghai Municipal Council lawyer Li Zhishan stated the previous events and requested an extension for investigation of the case. He presented the gun and bullets for inspection. When questioned by the defendants, their statements were evasive. Judge Xiao Xieffen ordered them to be remanded in custody for further review at a later date.

Annual Meeting of the China Corporation

The American China Corporation held its ninth annual shareholders' meeting at the company's office in Shanghai on February 20, 1935. The meeting was presided over by Vice Chairman Mr. Sadarley, who announced the following to the shareholders: "According to the established schedule, the time has come, and the shareholders and their representatives present represent a sufficient number of shares to meet the legal quorum. I would like to ask the company secretary to first read the notice of the annual shareholders' meeting." The secretary read: "Pursuant to the instructions of the company's board of directors, the China Corporation will hold its annual shareholders' meeting at 4:30 PM on Wednesday, February 20, 1935, at the company's office at No. 290 Sichuan Road, Shanghai. All stock transfer registration matters will be temporarily suspended from February 11 to February 20. All letters of proxy from shareholders must be submitted to the company's office before 5 PM on February 19 to be effective." Secretary Adam then reported: "1934 was the most difficult year I have ever experienced in Shanghai, especially for the real estate business. During the first nine months of last year, there was abundant money in the market, and interest rates were low, making it extremely difficult for our company to conduct mortgage business. It was even more difficult to collect commissions on this business. Unexpectedly, the financial market suddenly underwent a serious change, leading to a situation where money was not available for borrowing. In previous financial emergencies, it was still possible to borrow money at higher interest rates, but today it is not the case. Money has become impossible to access, and the value of collateral or the level of interest rates are insufficient as conditions for borrowing. As the saying goes, 'Things reach an extreme and then revert.' I hope that this is also the case for Shanghai today. This is because an article on the value of Shanghai real estate, published in the Economic and Commercial Gazette on January 9, 1935, shows that the value of Shanghai real estate has made considerable progress compared to other major cities around the world. Since real estate has been the guarantor of all property in the past, it must still maintain its primary position in future investment activities. This is what I am convinced of. Last year, the buying and selling of real estate in Shanghai was generally limited to special purposes, so the amount of transactions was very small. Given the general business situation and the current economic panic, I believe that the profits our company has earned last year are indeed satisfactory. All the directors of our company unanimously recommend setting aside a reserve fund and paying a dividend of one dime and five cents per share in accordance with American commercial law. This is because in the current situation and in the uncertain months of future market changes, it would be unwise to pay out dividends in excess of what is absolutely necessary. In short, although the current market is full of great dangers, we are convinced that once the market stabilizes, Shanghai's future will be optimistic, after we have exerted our best efforts in the face of all difficulties and maintained credit in Shanghai's real estate business. Before discussing the resolutions, if any shareholders have any questions, I am willing to do my best to answer them in detail." Resolution 1: "I propose to pass the 1934 business report and settlement." Mr. Li Wei seconded the motion. Passed. Resolution 2: "I propose to dispose of the remaining balance of 797,339 yuan, 8 jiao, and 2 fen listed in the profit and loss statement in the following manner: pay a dividend of 1 dime and 5 cents per share, totaling 75,000 yuan; establish and allocate a reserve fund of 500,000 yuan; and allocate the remaining balance of 222,339 yuan, 8 jiao, and 2 fen; totaling 797,339 yuan, 8 jiao, and 2 fen." Mr. Spier Monde seconded the motion. Passed. Resolution 3: "Mr. Ronis and Mr. Lin Yuting have voluntarily resigned from their positions as directors but are still eligible for candidacy." Proposed by Mr. Zhong Kecheng and seconded by Mr. Li Wei, they should still be recommended as directors for the next term. Passed. Resolution 4: "Proposed by Mr. Adam and seconded by Mr. Lin Yuting, we propose to hire Yi Maoli Accountants as the company's auditors for 1935." Passed.

Trafficking Ring Cracked

Wang Runhe and Zhang Faxiang, Chinese detectives from the Hongkou Police Station, learned that No. 105 North Jiangxi Road was a human trafficking center. At around 7 PM the day before yesterday, they secretly went there with foreign detectives, arrested the main culprit, Cantonese woman Ma A'mei, along with accomplices Jiang Yongqing from Tongzhou, Qiao Wengui from Jiangbei, Cantonese woman Wang Chenshi, and others, as well as opium smoking paraphernalia, and took them to the police station for detention. Yesterday morning, they were sent to the Third Criminal Court of the First Special District Court. Shanghai Municipal Council lawyer Li Zhishan stated that the defendant Ma A'mei had previously opened a brothel on Peng Road. In 1931, she had Jiang Yongqing abduct a girl named Wang Caigen from Wuxi to work as a prostitute at her place, for 170 yuan, for a term of four years. Last winter, when the term expired, she returned to her hometown. Recently, Jiang went to Wuxi again and had Wang come to Shanghai, staying at Gao Sanmei's place, a small sister, at No. 9 Jing'an Temple Road, intending to go to Ma A'mei's house again to continue her career as a divine maiden for profit. Jiang Yongqing, in collusion with Qiao Wengui, had abducted a six-year-old girl, Jin Di, and a thirteen-year-old girl, A'mei, both from Liyang, to Shanghai on January 22 of this year, and Wang Chenshi sold them to a certain Cantonese woman as adopted daughters for a total of 85 yuan. The suspects admitted to this at the police station. He requested an extension for a detailed investigation of the case. Then, Chinese and foreign detectives reported the course of the case investigation. Judge Xiao Xieffen questioned the defendants, whose statements were evasive. According to the testimony of women Wang Caigen and Gao Sanmei, the court ordered all defendants to be remanded in custody for further investigation at a later date.

Central Bank Inspection Report

The 224th Inspection Report on the Issuance Reserve of the Central Bank stated: "In accordance with Article 15 of the Central Bank Regulations, this council is responsible for inspecting the reserve for the issuance of convertible banknotes of the bank. The 224th inspection was held at the bank's Issuance Bureau on February 20, 1935. The results of the inspection are announced as follows: (A) The total amount of convertible banknotes issued is 90,037,277 yuan in silver, including 83,822,188 yuan in silver yuan notes and 6,215,089 yuan in subsidiary currency notes. The total amount of the convertible banknote reserve is 90,037,277 yuan, including 71,119,277 yuan in cash reserve. This cash reserve includes 67,214,295 yuan stored in the bank's Issuance Treasury, 2,141,980 yuan stored in branches in various ports, 1,833,002 yuan deposited with fellow banks, and a guarantee reserve equivalent to 19,180,000 yuan in silver yuan. (B) The total amount of customs gold convertible notes issued is 373,324 yuan and 7 jiao. The total amount of the customs gold convertible note reserve is 373,324 yuan and 7 jiao. This reserve includes 7,351 taels and 9 qian and 5 fen of gold bars, equivalent to 373,324 yuan and 7 jiao of customs gold at a fixed price of 5.0779. According to Article 2 of the Central Bank's Convertible Note Regulations, the cash reserve is 60% and the guarantee reserve is 40%. The results of this inspection show that the cash exceeds 60% and the guarantee reserve is less than 40%, which is in compliance with the regulations. This report is hereby issued." February 21, 1935, Li Fuxun, Chairman of the Board of Supervisors of the Central Bank, Supervisors Xie Mingxun, Bei Songsun, Qin Runqing, Yu Qiaqing, Lin Kanghou, Xu Jilong.

The Shanghai Asylum, affiliated with the China Mental Hospital on Dongyouheng Road, Hongkou District, has been highly effective in treating mental illness. Recently, more than ten patients have recovered and been discharged from the hospital. The Lao Jiuzhang Gongji Silk Store at the intersection of Nanjing Road and Shanxi Road, after taking over several million yuan worth of inventory from the previous management, held an unprecedented clearance sale. The existing inventory has now been cleared, and it is specifically scheduled to open officially tomorrow. The store has always been dedicated to revitalizing China's silk industry, so this time it has specially collected a large number of goods from famous domestic manufacturers across the country to meet the needs of all sectors of society. During the opening period, all goods will be specially discounted, and a large number of gifts, precious items, will be given away. Shanghai National Goods Company Opens Clearance Department

The Shanghai National Goods Company, located opposite the Hongmiao Temple on Nanjing Road, will implement scientific management cost accounting for each department starting on March 1. Departmental drawings have already been completed, and the monthly expenses of each department are specified in detail according to location, size, and number of people. Before the implementation of scientific management, the inventory of each department will be thoroughly sorted out, and goods that have been in stock for a long time and are of inferior quality will be selected. A clearance department will be specially set up on the second floor of the company starting on February 23, selling at the lowest prices. Each department will be equipped with new goods that are in season to meet the needs of all sectors of society.

Record of Shanghai Tobacco Exchange Industry Conference in North Shanghai

Since the new directors Chen Yaosheng, Mi Qinrui, and Yang Bingyi took office at the North Shanghai Office of the Shanghai Tobacco Exchange Industry Association, they have spared no effort in rectifying the association's affairs. At yesterday's regular meeting, the office noted that the Social Affairs Bureau had already inspected and approved the use of kerosene dispensers and issued a notice to comply. Fearing that some colleagues might not know about this and still use old dispensers, resulting in penalties, it was resolved that the office would purchase 100 sets of new dispensers and notify colleagues to purchase them at a cost to avoid penalties during inspections. Also, since the Stamp Tax Bureau is now starting to inspect stamp taxes, colleagues are urged to carefully check and affix stamps to avoid omissions.

City Sounds

Star Flower Dew Perfume in Short Supply: Since personnel from various regions have been sent to Shanghai to purchase Star Flower Dew Perfume, the Chinese and Western Pharmacy on Simalu, the general distributor, has felt the pressure of being in short supply. Unexpectedly, the South China region continues to purchase 1,000 boxes of large-sized bottles, which must be delivered within two weeks. The pharmacy is working day and night, but is still worried that it will not be able to meet the demand. The workers originally borrowed from the pharmaceutical department to jointly manufacture the product, but now that Tan Di and Wei Yao have accepted large orders, they had to withdraw them to the original factory. As a result, customers are complaining, and it is felt that it is difficult to cope with the demand. At the same time, it is also evident that the people of the country are enthusiastic about supporting domestic products.

All kinds of grand banquets are held there. In the past, there have been the Children's Relief Association Russian Ball and tomorrow's Washington Ball. The entertainment programs of the dance hall are also updated daily. They are changed every time they are performed. The Paramount Dance Troupe, which has caused a sensation in Shanghai, has newly staged "The Merry Widow," a film of Chinese waltzes, with colorful costumes and graceful dance steps. The new songs in the film "Spring Heart映媚" by Ke Wenpeilai are especially popular. Manager Tong Zugeng has been serving the community for many years and has a well-established reputation. The future development is predictable.

Recent News of the Expansion of the Xinguang Neon Company: The Xinguang Neon Company is the earliest Chinese-operated neon business. Since its founding, it has been in business for over eight years. It has always been praised by the society for its excellent products and faithful service. Most of the large neon projects in Shanghai and other ports are contracted by the company. Now, due to busy business, the original address at No. 58 Jiangxi Road is not enough for office space. The office has been moved to No. 161 Guangdong Road at the beginning of this year, and the factory has been moved to No. 66 Jiangxi Road, with a major expansion. According to the person in charge of the company, in addition to vigorously promoting the company's business in Shanghai this year, the company also plans to add branches and agencies in major ports across the country, in light of the frequent visits from customers from other ports, in order to achieve quick and efficient service. In addition to the branches already established in Pingjin, Beijing, and Jinan, the company is happy to contact established merchants who are willing to act as agents in other major ports.

National Goods Film Propaganda Agency Steps Up Work: The first film promoting domestic goods produced by the Chinese National Goods Film Propaganda Service Agency on Yunnan Road in Shanghai has been effective after the first propaganda team took it to Ningbo for promotion. Therefore, recently, several domestic goods factories and stores have come to request the production of similar films. In addition to actively preparing for the second filming project to serve various factories, the agency has also added a branch on Taodu Road in Ningbo and specially assigned personnel to be responsible for handling the contact matters there. It is learned that in order to expand the second filming project, the agency issued a letter today soliciting cooperation from various domestic goods factories and followed the precedent of the first time, offering 100 feet of film for free for every 300 feet or more produced, in order to express its service spirit.

Weather Report

The Xujiahui Observatory's weather forecast at 4:30 PM yesterday stated: "There is a strong cyclone in the East China Sea, with intermittent rain and fog. Zhejiang and the lower reaches of the Yangtze River are cloudy with fog and localized drizzling rain, but there is gradual improvement. Shandong and its surroundings are clear and cloudy, with winds from the north to northwest, or quite strong. The southern part and the Taiwan Strait are cloudy, with moderate seasonal winds. Also, within the 24 hours before 3:00 PM yesterday, the highest temperature in Shanghai was 51.8 degrees and the lowest was 44.4 degrees. On the same day last year, the highest temperature was 51.8 degrees and the lowest was 39.2 degrees."

Shortage of Agricultural Talents

Graduates of Jinling University's College of Agriculture All Have Jobs

(Nanjing, 21st dispatch) In recent years, many university graduates in various disciplines have been unable to find work. However, there is a shortage of agricultural talents, and all 18 graduates of Jinling University's College of Agriculture have jobs.

(1) Generalities, (2) Philosophy, (3) Religion, (4) Social Sciences, (5) Language, (6) Natural Sciences, (7) Applied Sciences, (8) Art, (9) Literature, (10) History and Geography, the total number is 3,951,847 volumes.

Solemn Declaration by the Italian Pen Club

The Pen Club is an organization of writers from various countries. At the international conference held in Scotland last year, there was a proposal that any writer who did not agree with the current political system of his country should also be a member of the Pen Club of that country. At that time, the Italian Pen Club was suspected of refusing to admit writers who opposed Fascism. Now, the President of the Italian Pen Club, Malinehi, sent a letter to the London International Pen Club, stating that no Italian writer in the entire world today expresses opposition to Fascist Italy. Therefore, in my capacity as President of the Italian Pen Club, I solemnly declare that this club welcomes any Italian writer to join as a member, regardless of their views. When this news reached London, it was precisely at a Pen Club dinner, and President H. G. Wells reported it to the public, and the crowd shouted "Long live Italy."

Jinan Municipal Government Adds Classes to Accommodate 2,000 Out-of-School Children

(Jinan, 21st dispatch) During the winter vacation, 2,000 students in this city were out of school because the schools could not accommodate them. The municipal government decided to order each school to add classes within two months to accommodate the remaining students in the city and is determined to ensure that all students are enrolled by the end of this year.

Feng County Government Ordered to Detain Qinyin's Acting Principal

(Bengbu, 21st dispatch) The Bengbu Qinyin Primary School has been experiencing a director change issue, with school board members criticizing the Education Bureau and the dispute escalating. The Feng County Government, upon provincial order, arrested the acting principal, Li Wencheng. Because Li disobeyed the order, he has been sent to the county for interrogation. The school board is asking for assistance from all sectors.

No Fisheries Specialty School in British Universities

The Sino-British Boxer Indemnity Board Replied to the Ministry of Education

The Sino-British Boxer Indemnity Board recently sent an official letter to the Ministry of Education stating that regarding the Ministry of Industry's request to set up fisheries quotas within the British examination period, because there are no fisheries specialty schools above the college level in the United Kingdom, it was not included. As for the establishment of fisheries internship quotas, the board will send a letter to the British Industries Confederation to look into it.

Four Organizations Jointly Prepare for Children's Painting Exhibition

Yesterday's First Preparatory Meeting Held

Organization Outline and Detailed Rules for Soliciting Works Approved

The Shanghai Municipal Bureau of Education, together with the Children's Happiness Association, the Children's Morning News, and the Chinese Art Education Society, in order to inspire children's intelligence and promote children's art, are jointly sponsoring a city-wide children's painting exhibition. It is scheduled to be held at Wuben, Shangwen, and Xicheng schools during this year's Children's Day, lasting for three days. Yesterday, the first preparatory meeting was held at the Municipal Education Center, where the organization outline and detailed rules for soliciting works were approved. Details are as follows:

Representatives Present: Zhang Meisun, Shi Chongpeng, and Shi Lianhuang from the Municipal Bureau of Education; Hu Shuyi and Qian Fugong from the Children's Morning News; Zhou Wanghe and Lu Yunkui from the Children's Happiness Association; Fu Boliang, Shi Wenbin, and Zhu Zhiwei from the Chinese Art Education Society, among others. Shi Chongpeng served as Chairman, and Qian Fugong as Recorder.

Matters Discussed: (1) Proposal to approve the organization outline: Approved with revisions. (2) Proposal to approve the detailed rules for soliciting works: Approved with revisions. (3) Proposal to approve the budget for this event: Resolved to limit it to 300 yuan, and Shuyi and Shi Chongpeng will draft a budget and request the Bureau of Education to allocate the funds. (4) How should the duties of this event be allocated?: Resolved: General Affairs Group - Bureau of Education; Solicitation Group - Bureau of Education & Art Education Society; Publicity Group - Children's Happiness Association & Children's Morning News; Review Group - Art Education Society. (5) Proposal to send a letter to the Bureau of Education requesting all elementary schools to submit works: Approved. (6) Proposal to solicit prizes from all parties: Resolved that the Children's Happiness Association will be responsible for handling this. (7) Proposal to hire judges: Resolved to invite Pan Gongzhan as the Chief Judge, and Jiang Danshu, He Mingzhai, Feng Zikai, Yu Jifan, Hu Shuyi, Zhang Chenbo, and Tang Guanyu as judges. (8) Discussion on borrowing venues: Resolved: To be handled by the Bureau of Education. (9) Proposal to designate the office of this event: Resolved to be located at the Bureau of Education.

Detailed Rules for Soliciting Works: (1) Scope: Sketches, pattern paintings, free paintings (limited to original works). (2) Submissions: Divided into two types: group and individual. (A) Group: Limited to municipal elementary schools and registered private elementary schools in Shanghai. The amount of submissions for each grade should be based on 1/10th of the number of students as the standard. (B) All children in Shanghai are welcome to participate freely. (3) Time: Submissions from various schools should be delivered to the designated locations from 9:00 AM to 5:00 PM on April 3rd: Senior grades to Wuben, middle grades to Shangwen, and lower grades (including kindergarten) to Xicheng. Self-arrangement, custody by the organizing committee, and registration of the number of pieces with receipts issued. After the closing of the exhibition, the works can be reclaimed with the receipts. Each school should also submit a list of submissions to the organizing committee for reference five days before the exhibition. (4) Awards: Excellent works will be awarded by the organizing committee and may be selected for publication in the Children's Morning News to encourage them.

Organization Outline: (1) This event is jointly initiated by the Shanghai Municipal Bureau of Education, the Children's Morning News, the Chinese Art Education Society, and the Children's Happiness Association, and is named the Shanghai Children's Painting Exhibition. (2) The purpose of this event is to inspire children's temperament, promote children's art, and assist in the progress of education. (3) This event will be organized by the above-mentioned initiating organizations, each sending one to three representatives to form a preparatory committee. (4) The preparatory committee may set up the following groups to carry out the work: General Affairs Group (including documents, affairs, arrangements, reception), Solicitation Group (including solicitation, custody), Review Group (including judges, awards), Publicity Group (including editing, publicity). (5) Each group will have a director, who will be concurrently appointed by the preparatory committee, and several staff members appointed by the preparatory committee. (6) For the convenience of handling matters, this event may hire one employee to be in charge of his affairs, and appropriate travel expenses will be given. (7) The exhibition period is set for three days from April 4th to 6th. (8) The exhibition venues are divided into three sections: senior grades, middle grades, and lower grades (including kindergarten), temporarily using Wuben, Xicheng, Shangwen schools, etc. as venues. (9) The solicitation of children's works mainly focuses on students from municipal elementary schools and registered private elementary schools in Shanghai. Detailed rules for soliciting works will be determined separately. (10) This event will hire experts to review the submissions, and prizes will be awarded to those with excellent performance. (11) Matters not covered in this outline may be revised by the preparatory committee.

The Science Society of China Continues to Offer the Miss Gao Memorial Award for Essay Submission

Essay Submission Period: From Now Until the End of October

This Year's Essay Topic Decided to be Chemistry

The Miss Gao Memorial Award, organized by the Science Society of China, has decided that this year's essay submissions will be on chemistry. The essay submission period is from now until October 31st. The Society has recently sent letters to various universities to start soliciting essays. Details are as follows:

Letter to Universities: The Society recently sent letters to renowned universities across the country, stating: "Dear Sirs, In order to promote scientific research among young people and to commemorate our late member, Miss Gao Junwei, we have specially established the Miss Gao Memorial Award, which solicits scientific essays annually. The scope of essay submissions for this year is limited to the field of chemistry. We are now sending several copies of the essay submission guidelines. We hope you will review them and publicize them so that students at your esteemed school can submit their research findings in a timely manner. We are sending this letter accordingly and hope that you will take note."

Essay Submission Guidelines: (1) The award consists of a gold medal from the Society and a cash prize of 100 yuan, which will be awarded to the top-ranked essay submission. Essays are solicited once a year. (2) The scope of essay topics is limited to the five subjects of natural science: mathematics, physics, chemistry, biology, and geology. The Society's Board of Directors will select one of the above five subjects each year on a rotational basis and organize an essay submission committee to oversee the solicitation and review of manuscripts.

Scope of Submission: (3) Students currently studying pure science and applied science at universities and specialized colleges in the country are eligible to participate in essay submissions. (4) Submissions should be essays on the subject specified for essay submission, with a word count of 3,000 to 10,000 words. The writing material should be substantial, novel, and accurate, and the writing should be clear, coherent, and accessible. Any texts that are plagiarized, translated, or have been published elsewhere will not be selected.

Essay Submission Deadline: (5) The 1935 essay submission will be limited to the field of chemistry. (6) The essay submission period for this year is from now until October 31st. After the essay is completed, it should be submitted to the "Miss Gao Memorial Award" Essay Submission Committee, Chinese Science Society, 533 Avenue Albert, Shanghai. (7) After the committee collects all the manuscripts, it will invite experts to assess them and determine the winning candidate, who will be announced in mid-December and awarded the prize and medal. (8) The winning essay submission will be published in the Society's journal "Science". (9) Essays that are not selected but are deemed valuable by the Society will be published in "Science" and will be given appropriate remuneration.

The Municipal Health Bureau and the Bureau of Education, in order to promote school health, are scheduled to convene principals and faculty members from various schools at 2:00 PM on the 24th of this month (Sunday) in Gaoqiao District to hold a health education discussion forum. Actively Preparing and Planning to Enroll Students in Early Next Month

The association originally planned to set up four groups: politics, economics, law, and literature, but for the time being, it plans to open a political class first, and expand it after it has been successful. World Book Company English Correspondence School

Special Fee Reduction Quota for Poor Students

Since the World Book Company's English Correspondence School advertised for enrollment, there has been a very enthusiastic response. It has recently been reported that the school has received letters from many poor students requesting consideration for their families' poverty and a reduction in tuition fees. The school, in view of the economic downturn, which is indeed a common phenomenon, and that poor students often have unfulfilled ambitions, which is a pity, has set up a fee reduction quota for poor students. It is reported that the measures are as follows: (1) Applicants must have a letter of certification from their parents or senior staff of their organization proving that they are indeed poor students. (2) After the school verifies that they are indeed poor, the tuition fees will be reduced to 12 yuan for the elementary level, 16 yuan for the intermediate level, and 20 yuan for the advanced level. Those who pay in installments will also receive a corresponding reduction in proportion to the above.

"We are on the road to cultivation, do not confine ourselves, do not stop lecturing, do not stop learning, should we visit each other to observe the community and cut and saw each other."
