Special Report

Pan Gongzhan's Lecture on Shanghai's School Education (4)

(II) We not only hope that all school-age children have the opportunity to attend primary school, but we also want to find ways to provide educational opportunities for illiterate adults. This "adult education" is called "adult education" in foreign countries. "Adult education" in foreign countries is remedial education for those older people who lack specialized knowledge. These people have all received primary education in their childhood. They say that losing education at an older age is definitely not like our people who, when they get older, do not even know how to read. Perhaps some countries also have illiterate older people, but such people are always in the minority. We should always find ways to teach the generally illiterate older people in our country to read a little, even if it is just a few words, it is better than not knowing any. We usually call this kind of education "mass education," but as I see it, the four words "mass education" are somewhat inappropriate. Why? Since it is called "mass education," then all the masses should be included. As far as the "masses" are concerned, not only are older people who are illiterate the masses, but also primary school students, middle school students, and university students are also the masses. All education is received by the masses. In reality, it should still be called "adult education," but for the time being, we don't need to worry about this name. It is also acceptable to continue using "mass education," but it should be divided into adult and children's departments, targeting illiterate adults and children. So, what is the situation of "adult education," that is, "mass education," in Shanghai? I can briefly report it. I won't talk about the "mass schools" established privately in Shanghai. The municipal "mass schools" have now been held for thirteen sessions, each session graduating in four months. They have been held thirteen times in a row. In the first session, there were twenty schools. In the second session, there were thirty schools. In the third session, there were thirty-three schools. In the fourth session, there were thirty-five schools. In the fifth session, there were fifty-two schools. In the sixth session, there were fifty-two schools. In the seventh session, there were fifty-four schools. In the eighth session, there were thirty-five schools. In the ninth session, there were forty-three schools. In the tenth session, there were forty-six schools. In the eleventh session, there were fifty-one schools. In the twelfth session, there were fifty schools. The schools in the twelfth session will not graduate until January 1935. The thirteenth session held fifteen "higher mass schools." These students will not graduate until March 1935. Except for the student numbers in the thirteenth session, which have not been statistically compiled, the total number of students, both male and female, in the previous twelve sessions is 23,336. Because the books and other supplies of the "mass schools" are given to the students, they often stop coming after studying for only a few days. Therefore, some students stop coming to school before graduating. As a result, the number of students who completed four months and graduated in the twelve sessions is only 10,126, averaging less than 1,000 students per session. Up to the eleventh session, the expenses used by the "mass schools" totaled 52,013 yuan, averaging about 5,000 yuan per session, which means that each graduate costs 5 yuan. The expenses used to run "mass schools" are much less compared to primary schools. Moreover, the funds we use to promote "mass education" are mostly from the surplus money from running primary and secondary school education, so there is actually not much special funding for promoting "mass education." In short, for the generally illiterate older people, we want to enable them to know some basic characters and understand some common knowledge. This is the minimum simple knowledge that everyone should know. However, if we extrapolate based on the progress ratio of running mass schools in the past, to provide literacy education to all one million (approximate number) adult illiterates in Shanghai, we need to run another one thousand sessions of mass schools. At four months per session, it will take four thousand months, which is equivalent to more than three hundred years. In terms of funding, each graduate of a mass school costs 5 yuan of public funds, then the literacy funding for these one million illiterates would reach 5 million yuan. Isn't that shocking? It can be seen that using this old method of running mass education to carry out universal education is really laughable. We must find other ways for this poor China and poor Shanghai.

Originally, "elementary education" focuses on teaching children basic characters and common knowledge, and "mass education" also focuses on teaching adults basic characters and common knowledge. Therefore, these two types of schools should be interconnected, and our future approach will be to use large, medium, and small schools as the foundation for promoting "mass education." All primary and secondary school teachers should participate in promoting "mass education." At the same time, we should also encourage university students, middle school students, and older primary school students to do this work together. In addition to studying themselves, they should take some time to teach illiterate people. In this way, both learning and teaching will not only improve their own studies, but also serve as a way to repay society. If we take a look at all the students in the city, there are currently more than 150,000 primary school students. If we find one older student out of ten primary school students, there will be 15,000 people. Add to that 32,000 middle school students and 12,000 university students, and the total comes to 59,000 people, almost 60,000 people. Add to that about 12,000 faculty and staff from all levels of schools. If these 60,000 students and 12,000 faculty and staff all make a vow to be responsible for teaching three "illiterates" to read this semester, whether they are teaching villagers or the old maids at home, anyone who is illiterate can be taught. In this way, after half a year, 72,000 people can teach 210,000 people and eliminate 210,000 "illiterates." This is definitely not wishful thinking. The reason we are suffering now is because we have not done it. If we all make a determination to do it, taking a few hours each week or some time each day to do this is not a difficult task. This is not an impossible task like "carrying Mount Tai to cross the North Sea." Everyone is not doing it because they don't want to, not because they can't. If we can do it according to this calculation, we can teach 210,000 people in half a year, and 400,000 people in a year. Naturally, it will not take two or three years to eliminate all the "illiterates" in Shanghai. Moreover, we must also have a method. Regardless of men, women, old, or young, whoever teaches a literate person should make an agreement with them. We teach you without taking your money, and you should also make a vow that after you learn to read, you will voluntarily be responsible for teaching one or two illiterate people. In this way, if we teach 210,000 people in the first semester, by the second semester, we will teach more than just 210,000 people, because if each of the 210,000 newly literate people in the first semester also goes to teach one more person, wouldn't we be able to teach 400,000 people in the second semester? If we do it like this, we will definitely be able to eliminate "illiteracy." However, this method requires everyone to vigorously promote it and "put it into practice." Don't think of it as a fantasy. Even if we don't succeed completely, it's still better than not doing it. If you think about it, I was always taught by my parents and teachers. Now I am fulfilling my duty to teach three people to read, which is also a way to repay society. Moreover, a few literacy primers don't cost much money. Even if I buy three copies and give them to the students, it is very important. China is a "poor country," so we must "calculate frugally." Just because people are poor, does that mean they don't do anything? We must talk about efficiency, use less money, and achieve great results. I sincerely hope that people who have already received education and students who are still in school, regardless of age, can all make a vow to contribute their strength to "adult education," and it is best to start doing it now. Don't wait, thinking that if you don't do it today, there is still tomorrow. When January 1st of next year comes, thinking that there are still 365 days, you can't wait "until next year." Moreover, the world situation is changing unpredictably. We cannot wait, nor can we afford to wait.

Perhaps some people will ask, the things you are lecturing on today are all very superficial. Even if young children know some basic common sense and older illiterates know a few characters, what great use is there? People can invent airplanes and fly them, and people can invent poison gas and manufacture guns and cannons. If we don't pay attention to these issues, won't we still suffer? Therefore, a "problem" arises. Some people say that "specialized education" is the most important and that "primary education" and "adult education" should both be categorized under "universal education." As a result, China has had two schools of thought in the past. As I just said, it seems like I am standing on the "universal education" line. There are also many famous scholars who seem to look down on "universal education," thinking that "specialized talents" are important. But my meaning is not that we don't need "specialized talents," but that "universal education" is particularly important at this time. This is from a comparative perspective. I remember that from the late Qing Dynasty to the early Republic of China, these two opinions were debated a lot.

Spring and Autumn

Tidbits

— (Jiaoxin)

Whenever the night before it snows, the drunkards always want to invite two or three close friends to have a few drinks. Bai Juyi's line, "Late, the sky threatens snow, could we drink a cup or no?" is indeed a vivid portrayal; but those who do not drink cannot appreciate its beauty.

Women always want to manage their husbands so that they are completely obedient, obeying their wives' commands; but they absolutely do not want their sons to listen to their wives. Women always say how bad their daughters-in-law are, but their daughters are always good no matter what; if they marry unhappily and there is discord between the mother-in-law and daughter-in-law, then of course it is the mother-in-law's fault. So women's psychology is extremely contradictory.

Prison

— Yan Chonglou

The wounds on my legs deepen, the shackles tighten; the wounds on my back increase, the contact with the whip becomes more frequent;

Sweat washes the long hair on my pale head, my beard grows full on my sallow face, outside there is a free world—but it is only separated by a solid iron window.

This little poem is what I used to lament prisoners. When a person unfortunately falls into prison, his happiness is completely deprived!

But although life inside the iron window is miserable, can the world outside the iron window be considered free? In comparison, there are no shackles, no beatings with whips; but countless invisible and heavy shackles, one by one invisible and poisonous whips, are all over this turbulent era, attacking all of humanity without mercy.

Look: those who commit suicide for economic reasons, are they not sacrificing themselves in the prison of money? Those who take their own lives for marriage, are they not destroyed in the prison of love? Those who are pessimistic about life because of superstition, are they not ruined in the prison of religion? ... People fall, suffer, scream, and struggle in various prisons; therefore, the boundary between tangible and intangible prisons is very small!

Prisoners in this vast prison! Concentrate all your enthusiasm and ambition, and create a truly free and happy new world.

Youtiao Anecdotes

— Yan He

Previously, I read Mr. Wang Shaba's "Youtiao Anecdotes," which said, "I happened to hear a comedian on the radio singing a song about dabing and youtiao: Dabing youtiao, dabing youtiao, blow wheat flowers, blow wheat flowers,..." After checking, this song was actually the song "Down with the Powers, Down with the Powers, Eliminate the Warlords, Eliminate the Warlords, the National Revolution is Successful, the National Revolution is Successful, Let's Sing Together! Let's Sing Together!" which was widely sung after the Northern Expeditionary Army arrived in Shanghai in 1927. At that time, someone imitated this song and created "Dabing Youtiao, Dabing Youtiao, Crispy Youtiao, Crispy Youtiao, Three Coppers a Piece, Three Copper Coins a Piece, Cheap or Not? Cheap or Not?" These two songs were both popular at the time, and even the common people could sing them. It didn't need a "certain comedian" to "break new ground."

The three words "blow wheat flowers" are the most egregious invention. Are they drawing on Du Fu's poem, "Fine wheat falls with light flowers," or Duan Maotang's saying, "North of the river, wheat blooms like a painting, a yang object, so eating it strengthens the body: south of the river, wheat blooms at night, a yin object, so eating too much harms people," as the basis for wheat flowers? But what does the word "blow" mean? Undoubtedly, this is the "sesame oil fried dough twists" and "crispy youtiao" that street vendors are selling.

Youtiao is also known as Korean sticks. These names are only seen in colloquial language, and there is very little basis for them in books. Rural women insert a silver needle into their hair bun, and the needle is wound into a youtiao shape, which is called a youtiao needle. There are also silver bracelets worn on the arm, wound into a youtiao shape, which are also called youtiao bracelets. As for the word "crispy" in "crispy youtiao," it is an adjective used by the seller.

In the past, someone imitated the poem "Peach Blossom Face" to praise youtiao, saying: "Last year today, I passed this door, Pitted faces knead youtiao opposite each other, the pitted face doesn't know where it went, the youtiao is still fried in the oil pot." It is truly irresistibly amusing.

Also, the Fujian Miscellaneous Records says: "What the Fujianese call youguo is the youzhuokuai of Hangzhou. The Fuzhou people also call it youzhuokuai, while the Xinghua people only call it zhuokuai." According to this, it is the commonly known youzhaokuai.

The Three Giants of World Politics

— Zuo

A Quick Sketch of the Life of Shanghai Beggars

— Zhang Muliang

Beggars in Shanghai are not only not decreasing, but are increasing day by day; perhaps this is because their life is idyllic?

Indeed, the sky is their quilt, the ground is their bed. They lie down and have a dream, carefree and incomparable. As the saying goes, "Begging for three years, I don't want to be an official." The idyllic life of beggars can be said to be perfectly described!

Beggars in this chilly season are no longer happy to wrap themselves in burlap sacks, hug messy thatch, torn paper, and sleep in the small alleys under the overhanging buildings, eating the northwest wind with their cold friends. Because their daily income is about two to three thousand cash, they will also borrow inns to go to; these inns are concentrated in the French Concession area, like behind Gongguan Road, north of Baxianqiao, Dongxinqiao, and the old Beimen area, there are inns that specialize in beggars' business? The rooms in these inns are not like the rooms in large hotels, with water heaters, sofas, tables, and chairs...fully equipped, they are all rooms divided into small cubicles, just enough for one person to sleep in, commonly called "pigeon cages." The price of this "pigeon cage" style room is generally from more than ten copper coins to more than thirty copper coins per night. Several old hands even smoke opium and play poker at night. When they are hungry, they order a few plates of egg fried rice to eat. This is their usual thing and is not surprising.

When it dawns, general seasoned beggar, with a cigarette butt clipped in between his fingers, walks along and asks for alms from pedestrians. They also often shout "catching pigs," isn't this a novel approach? There are also beggars who beg from all kinds of families. If they see the door of a house open, they will visit, and they will say in their mouths: "It's been a long time since I've come!" This is probably meant to be polite?

Little Western Heaven

— Written by Zhang Henshui

Chapter Nine: Inept at Flattery, Seeking Help Meets Rebuff; Unable to Return, Misled by Exaggerated Claims

"Small-footed woman"—these four words clearly reached her ears, and she couldn't help but interject, laughing: "What does that matter? Even though we have small feet, we can do anything. If I were to kneel on the ground and work, you big-footed women wouldn't do as much as I do." That woman came from the East and was steeped in civilized education. People didn't call her "Madam," but "Mr." or "Ms." No one had ever addressed her with "you" and "we" in that way. Instantly, her face turned red, and she waved her hand towards the door: "Go away! You don't understand any manners. I don't need someone like you. Go away!" After saying that, she waved her hand twice more. Although Madam Hu didn't understand her words, she understood the repeated "go away." Since she was being told to go away, the promise of work was off the table. Her heart had been full of hope, believing that meeting the owner would provide an opportunity to eat her fill, but she didn't expect that the Western-style woman would have such a temper, turning red in the face after only a few words. She didn't know what she had done wrong, but she couldn't bear losing the opportunity to work immediately, so she said: "Oh! Weren't you looking for help?" As she spoke, she felt somewhat flustered. Naturally, her two feet were unsteady, and her body swayed back and forth. The woman waved her hand again: "Get out of here! Who needs a useless person like you to work?" When Cheng Zhiqian saw the woman lose her temper at first, he didn't really mind. But now that she was telling the woman to "get out," even though the poor woman couldn't resist, her impolite manner embarrassed even the introducer. He reddened and said to Yueying: "Your mother really doesn't know how to speak; she can't get a welcome out of anyone she meets. Let's help your mother go back." (139)

Records of Fleeting Fragrance

— Originally written by Princess Der Ling of the Qing Dynasty, translated by Qin Shouou

Furthermore, to our delight, the person who arrived to tidy up before us had also noticed the stage. As a result, the pillars on the stage had already been repainted, and the flying dragons carved on the pillars had been uniformly coated with a layer of gold paint, dazzlingly bright and eye-catching. Now, with a few embroidered silk curtains hung up, the stage instantly had a fresh look. It was like a country bumpkin putting on a new gown; while his inherent rustic and foolish demeanor couldn't be completely hidden, at least it wouldn't be so offensive to the eye! The Empress Dowager nodded and smiled, indicating that the stage could still be used. So, could our opera begin? Not quite yet! To start the opera, the Empress Dowager herself had to give the order. No one dared to act without authorization. At the moment, the Empress Dowager was enthusiastically telling us how Yang Silang was lost in a foreign land, how he married Princess Iron Mirror, how he longed for his family, how the princess stole the order for him, and how he crossed the border… She was determined not to let us stop halfway through any of the details, so the opera was put on hold. It wasn't until she finished telling the story of how Yang Silang returned too late, causing Empress Xiao to find out and almost have him executed, but Princess Iron Mirror saved him, that the story finally ended.

Once she stopped talking, everyone knew that the opera was about to begin. She didn't need to say anything; she just waved her hand, and a eunuch rushed to the edge of the stage like a flying arrow, loudly announcing: "The Old Buddha has decreed: Start the opera!" In an instant, the stage was filled with the sounds of gongs and drums, and scene after scene unfolded. Even while the opera was being performed, the Empress Dowager wouldn't be quiet, constantly telling us about the various customs and anecdotes of the opera. In reality, it was because she had seen so many operas that she couldn't sit quietly and watch peacefully anymore. (250)

Itinerary

A Glimpse of the Ueno Zoo in Japan (Part 1)

— Ji Yun

The Ueno Zoo in Ueno Park is the largest in Japan. Not only in Japan, but perhaps also the largest in East Asia. For a ticket price of 15 cents, you can spend the whole day there and see animals from all over the world on display.

In the section for land mammals, there are buffaloes, camels, mules, horses, etc. Among them, there is a brown steed with a sign saying that it had been to Fengtian, Harbin, and Inner Mongolia, participating in races and traveling over 1,800 li. Foxes, wolves, bears, etc., which are more ferocious, are all kept in iron cages. Various kinds of deer, sheep, and pigs are only surrounded by short iron railings.

Two Indian gray elephants are the largest figures in the zoo, and their residence occupies a large Western-style house. During the day, they can also go to the nearby open space for a walk. They have no tusks. They often stretch their long noses out of the iron cage, soliciting food from the audience. In front of each animal, there is a wooden box containing a pot of food, such as sweet potatoes and radishes. The box lid is labeled "One cent per pot." Many children throw food to the animals. Although there is no one supervising, they can put the money in the small cabinet properly.

There are few natural stones in Ueno Park, but animals like to live in the wild. So they use artificial stones to create high mountains and steep peaks, just like the artificial mountains in our country, which are quite realistic. The mountain cave where dozens of monkeys live has peaks three or four zhang high, and waterfalls of tap water flow gurglingly, like the Mountain of Flowers and Fruit in "Journey to the West."

Polar bears, seals, and sea lions are animals from the Arctic Ocean, so there are seawater pools next to them to make their lives comfortable. Hippos live in indoor swimming pools with hot water supplied by radiators. Because it has been very cold these past few days, the two hippos are always hiding at the bottom of the water, only sticking their nostrils out of the water every 20 or 30 minutes to get air.

Various exotic birds are separated by wire cages that are two or three zhang high. Inside, there are evergreen trees for them to perch on, so they are not in a state of freedom. All waterfowl have small ponds where they can swim, so their feathers are very clean and shiny. However, the tail feathers of some white peacocks and bluebirds are stained with mud, and they are broken, with only a few left.

The most difficult to feed are of course tropical animals. The climate in Japan is colder than in Shanghai, China, so they spare no effort to build warm rooms and use radiators to provide heat. Various beautiful little birds occupy a large room. The method of raising fish is very special. The tanks are made of glass to prevent water leakage. The bottom of the tanks is covered with fine sand and pebbles, and stones with moss growing on them. Submerged aquatic plants are also planted, so that various kinds of fish can live comfortably. The glass tanks are built into the wall, and light is shone down from above, so that viewers can clearly see the fish swimming back and forth in the seaweed. They also use mechanical ingenuity to keep the water in the tanks constantly flowing, and the water volume is neither too much nor too little.

New York Stock Market Hit by Recovery Act

According to a report from New Feng Foreign Firm, yesterday (the 20th), the New York stock market trended weak. After President Roosevelt submitted the Recovery Act's message, railway and public utility stocks softened first, and the market then fell by 1 to 3 yuan. The income of public utility companies is generally regulated, so they suffered the most from the Recovery Act. Although the income of railways is also regulated, fortunately, industry regulations have not yet been formulated, but increased costs, such as increased wages for workers and rising material prices, will also cause considerable harm. When the selling spread to industrial stocks, steel, automobile, and entertainment stocks were the first to suffer. American Telephone & Telegraph Company announced that it would continue to pay a dividend of 2 yuan and 2 jiao and a half per share, which had a considerable stabilizing effect on the market. The bond market followed the downstream trend of U.S. government bonds, the latter's softening was largely a reaction after the rise. The small exchange's stock market fell due to the selling of public utility stocks. Chicago wheat fell sharply due to speculation by speculators. The total daily trading volume was 970,000 shares. The Dow Jones Index is listed on the left.

Therefore, amidst the fluctuations, there was a slight firming trend. Until the afternoon opening, the current month turned stable due to the continued purchases by customer gangs. The forward months saw very clear trading, and buyers were slightly quiet, so the market atmosphere slightly softened. The subsequent situation, if there are no special changes in imported wheat, should be seen as a stable situation. As a result, February and March were unchanged, April was down by a small 2.5 li, May was down by a small 7.5 li, and June and July were down by a small 2.5 li.

Future Wheat Shows a Softening Trend Amidst Fluctuations

Yesterday, the future wheat market, after the morning and afternoon openings, each month generally showed a stagnant and weak trend. In terms of imported wheat quotations, Chicago fell by about 3, 4, or 5 jiao, and Canada fell by 1 jiao and 6 fen. At the time of opening, trading in each month was light and dull. Because the market situation was very complex, given the trend of spot imported wheat, the market atmosphere could not turn bullish. However, after being too low, factories naturally had a purchasing trend, so it could not be suppressed too much. Therefore, amidst the fluctuations, only a slight decline was seen. As a result, the current month was down by 1 fen, March was down by 3 fen, and April was down by 2 fen. In the spot wheat market, due to the mills' good appetite, high-quality goods remained stable, while medium and lower-quality goods loosened slightly. Kaiyingzhou wheat was priced at 3 yuan and 9 jiao and 3 or 4 fen, Bengbu wheat was priced at 3 yuan and 9 jiao, and Gaoyou wheat was priced at 3 yuan and 8 jiao and 7 or 8 fen, totaling 3,800 bales, which were purchased by Shen Da, it is said.

Overseas wheat, the export situation in Canada shows no signs of improvement. Some Winnipeg locals are selling off, and there is hope only if there is progress in commercial needs.

River Rice Arrivals and Sales are Both Weak

(South Shanghai) Yesterday, the sources for each gang were even less, totaling only a little over ten houses. Arrivals and sales were both sparse, and the market situation was stable. The prices of each thick japonica rice showed no ups or downs. Late rice was also similar. Only those from Zhongguan were relatively lacking in arrivals, and there was some movement in bag orders, seemingly slightly brightening. Shade-dried Yuan rice continued to be unchanged, and Duyang pointed rice had no market. It is estimated that bag orders included 400-500 bales from the Beijing and Yantai gangs, and 300-400 bales of stacked goods.

(North Shanghai) Yesterday, there were a little over ten sources from the river. Light rain fell continuously. The transactions of various goods on the market were minimal. The price of medium-quality shade-dried Yuan rice was close to a chi. Thin rice was continuously consumed and converted. The debt conversely fell by a small 1 jiao. Yangjian rice sales were stagnant for days. The price had a small fall. Otherwise, prices were generally stable. Only small-price white japonica rice was not abundant in the market, and the appetite was still movable. The price was 5 or 6 fen higher.

Customer Indica Rice Prices are High and Sales are Sluggish

Selling Prices Fluctuate

Yesterday, the situation in the foreign customer indica rice market was mixed. After consecutive days of price increases in customer indica rice, importers became hesitant and were constrained by lower-quality foreign rice and broken foreign rice, so customer indica rice could not rise any further. However, the production price was high, and subsequent batches were difficult to transport. Yesterday morning, only bag orders were unopened. In the afternoon, the interior purchased 2,148 bags of brown rice and 100 bags of machine oil. The price was similar to the previous market. The consumption of foreign rice in the interior was still active. Yesterday, 30 bags of Sai Gon No. 3 and 5,600 bags of broken rice were purchased from the interior. This street also purchased 3,300 bags of high-quality Sai Gon and Siamese machine rice. The price of No. 3 and broken rice continued to rise by 5 or 6 fen. Round-grain high-quality Sai Gon rice had few arrivals, and the price rose by nearly 1 jiao. Long-grain Sai Gon rice had sufficient inventory and arrivals, and conversely fell by a small 5 fen, it is said.

Soybeans Turn Up 5 Fen

Yesterday, the soybean market situation, with a lively factory appetite and optimistic sentiment, turned up by 5 fen. Hankou beans also had a tight trend of 2 or 3 fen. Yesterday, it was estimated that factories purchased a total of three truckloads of whole river beans, priced at 3 yuan, 9 jiao, 2 fen and 9 jiao. In this street, the interior purchased over 350 bags of Shashi beans, priced at 3 yuan and 4 jiao and 7 fen. Over 1,500 bags of Hankou Zha beans, priced from 3 yuan and 5 jiao and 8 fen to 5 jiao.

Free Talk

Various Aspects of Humanity

— Bai Zhu

Masks, broadly speaking, can be divided into two types.

George Bernard Shaw, in one of his plays, used the words of a stone man to satirize the world: "In every concert in England, you can see countless rows of bored people who are there not because they really like classical music, but because they think they should like it. The same thing happens in the Kingdom of Heaven. Many people are sitting there gloriously not because they are happy, but because they feel that for the sake of decency, they have to sit there. Almost all of them are British." These witty words are truly a wake-up call to the hypocritical and reserved people of the world. In our lives, we don't know how many such people we can encounter. They wear masks and build their own fortresses with lies and evasions. They have never not known that they are fake, but in order to maintain their own identity and interests, they have to succumb to these masks and walk into the tomb. Courteous dealings, dignified and serene demeanor, inside these may be lurking the most despicable fraud in the world. "When the host says 'advance,' then they bow twice and deliberately delay getting up. When they get up, they present longevity money to the host. If the host deliberately refuses to accept it, then they insist. If the host deliberately refuses to accept it firmly, then they insist again. Only then does he order the official to accept it. Then they bow twice again, and again deliberately delay getting up. When they get up, they perform five or six bows before leaving." These actions of hosts and guests yielding and retreating simply constitute a wonderful "human comedy." In addition, when lovers meet, whispering sweet nothings, they say something like: "How can I leave you!" This is all too much like acting. If we sit down and think about it carefully, we can't help but laugh silently.

However, besides these, masks also appear in human life in another form. This is not the pillar of a gentleman's demeanor, but a forced affectation under the whip of a ruthless life. The waitresses in hotels, the dancers in dance halls, the prostitutes in the red light district, the low-level employees who watch the faces of their superiors, the impoverished households who try to keep up appearances, and the merchants who force themselves to smile. Although their lives are filled with countless festering sores, they still have to wear their masks in order to live. They have to smile when they meet people, have to have charming eyes, and have to have respectful manners. These are just superficial phenomena on the surface of their lives. Only when we dig deep into the roots can we know that all of this is fake, just like a few bright flowers and plants on a ruin, or a few pleasant musical sounds beside a dead person's coffin. In this art of dealing with the world, where people's joys and sorrows are different and where people's feelings are controlled by others, there is truly buried a deep and incomparable human flavor. If you are not a superficial observer, you will read from the ingratiating smiles that fear not being favored by others, from the fawning smiles that fear not grasping the other party, and from the forced smiles that fear being seen as weak, the tearful and blurred pleas of a heart squeezed under the heavy grinding of life. This state of mind of seeking joy in poverty and seeking laughter in tears soon turns into a complete paralysis, and even wearing a mask without realizing it, moving vaguely like a ghost. Such characters can often be seen in Russian novels. In a short story by Andreyev entitled "Laughter," he writes about a person who wears a funny mask to a dance party to meet the lover who abandoned him. He says: "Wherever I go, a burst of laughter surrounds me. It is with me, and I cannot escape this circle of revelry... But how lonely I am under this mask!" Later, when he left the venue and walked onto the street, his friend, while praising him for being interesting, saw that he had scratched his mask and suddenly realized: "By God, he was actually crying!" That's right, he had been crying all along.

Although these two types of masks are different, they are both deformed characters created by this deformed society. When will people throw their masks into the trash heap? When will people be able to live a better life?

The Content and Form of Scientific Essays

— Ren Baige

Literature and science have always had a strict boundary. According to the classification of scholars in the past, it was generally believed that literature is figurative description, focusing on sensibility, and science is abstract explanation, focusing on reason. Thus, they were clearly separated both in form and content. Now, once we want to unite them well, there will naturally be many difficulties. However, judging from the existing attempts, it is not entirely without merit. As long as our writers are willing to work hard, they will of course get satisfactory results. Here, I will briefly talk about the cultivation of our writers.

In the past, because literature and science had a strict boundary, writers mostly could only be writers or scholars in one field. Writers often lacked a scientific mind, and scientists often lacked literary skill. It is rare to find a writer like G.H. Wells who wrote many historical and scientific stories in a literary style and tone. Therefore, it is really very difficult to find a writer who truly possesses both a scientific mind and literary skill. Naturally, so-called scientific essays are not easy to produce. Recently, on the one hand, due to the growth of new literary theories, a literary artist must have a scientific perspective whether in criticism or creation. On the other hand, because literary works are relatively easy to access by the public, scientists who generally approach the public have had to apply literary forms to introduce science to the public. Thus, literature and science have had a possible unity. It is not accidental that scientific essays are produced at this time. To write good scientific essays, needless to say, the prerequisite is that it must be a person who truly possesses both a scientific mind and literary skill. Shouldn't our writers who often write scientific essays pay special attention to such cultivation?

How should one cultivate oneself? Objectively speaking, since so-called scientific essays are the unity of science and literature, subjectively speaking, it should be a kind of comprehensive research and learning. Science cannot be separated from the explanation of laws, and literature cannot be separated from the description of typical examples. Moreover, this is very important. The so-called comprehensive research and learning lies in enabling writers to cultivate the ability to use scientific knowledge and literary skills to depict and explain every thing and law in a typical way. As long as one has this kind of ability, I believe that the scientific essays produced will certainly be more impressive. Directly speaking, this is to require our writers to simultaneously possess scientific and literary cultivation in a unity, and to unite these two kinds of cultivation. As for what scientific and literary cultivation is, it is unnecessary to say more.

Saying this, it is probably not very clear. Here, it is better to cite another example. For example, how should a scientific essay with the theme of "firefly" be written correctly? In a person who has both scientific and literary cultivation, he first extracts the points that need to be explained scientifically, and then describes them according to literary methods. The main thing about the depiction of characters in literature is the typical among the general. Except for being used as a symbol of identity and an explanation of personality and state of mind, all static external descriptions are dispensable. Describing the ears and mouth of a certain person and the clothes that a certain person is wearing in every detail is ultimately the method of old novels, and that era has long passed. Applying this concretely to scientific essays means that when writing about "fireflies," there is no need to spend a lot of ink describing how beautiful its firefly is. Instead, one should mainly describe the story of a firefly from its occurrence and development, form and characteristics, and its relationship to human society. Other things can be inferred by analogy. I wonder if the writers who currently write scientific essays generally agree with this opinion?

Speaking only of the scientific essays currently written by general writers, it is true that, as some people have said, many are either like a lesson in a textbook or put too much emphasis on the formal aspects, and they only pay attention to natural science but not social science. To remedy this shortcoming, I do not object to some of the things that people have proposed to write. However, I think that it is not very appropriate to belittle the "literary art" of scientific essays and their role in breaking superstitions. We are still in a period of experimentation, and we should have considerable tolerance and generosity towards the scientific essays published in magazines. Because at least it is a progress to turn something useless in essays into something useful.

Casual Talks on Historical Essays (2)

— Cao Juren

The first one I wrote was about Fan Zeng. It took the story of Fan Zeng being alienated by Xiang Yu and dying of an ulcer on his back on the way back to Pengcheng as its theme. The center was the shadow of an intellectual being abandoned by a sword hilt. It was entitled "Ya Wen" and published in "Literary Monthly." Looking back now, I loved to lengthen the article too much, and it was no longer a historical essay. Later, I changed my own method, focusing on injecting new feelings, and using historical events as examples to explain a certain consciousness. Then I began to write the two short stories "Jesus and Christ" and "Su Xiaoxiao and the White Snake." At that time, I first wanted to criticize a certain event in reality, and use historical events to elaborate. Occasionally, I could express the sadness in my heart, but I inevitably distorted the original appearance of the historical events, so it could not be regarded as a standard historical essay. Sometimes I had deep feelings, but in the eyes of the readers, they were treated as lighthearted old stories. Therefore, I didn't want to write this kind of trivial play about entrusting ancient times with my feelings anymore, and I made up my mind to try to write standard historical essays. The death of Mi Heng was my attempt. Other short stories written before and after include Ye Mingchen, Liu Zhen Ping Zhu (see "New Novel"), and the Burning Grass Incident (semi-monthly "Mangzhong").

When I first started writing, I often had the illusion that I couldn't write without a complete story. Later, I gradually realized that whether the story was complete or not was secondary. How to organize the story was the most important thing. Mi Heng has a biography in the "Book of the Later Han." He relied on his talent and was arrogant, and could not be tolerated by Cao Cao, Liu Biao, or Huang Zu. In the poems praising Parrot Island throughout history, many blamed Cao Cao and Huang Zu, saying that they could not tolerate genius. I looked at the entire biography carefully and felt that Mi Heng's death was not due to Cao Cao and Huang Zu being jealous of his talent, but due to Cao Cao. The left and right people of Huang Zu should be able to depict this point of view as the center. At the end of the biography, the two sentences "Zu usually hated Heng, and immediately killed him" clearly broke this cause, while the previous text "Cao was angry, ... sent him to Liu Biao, ... before leaving, everyone sent him off, ... all used insults that he did not get up ...", "Biao once drafted a memorial with the literary men, and used his talents, but when Heng came back and saw it, he destroyed it by throwing it on the ground before he even finished reading it, and Biao was stunned. Heng then asked for pen and paper, and composed it in a moment. The wording was admirable, and Biao was very happy and respected him even more." In the lines, there was vaguely a situation where the left and right people harbored resentment and jealousy and helped the master to drive away guests. I reversed the order and reorganized the story. Huang She (Huang Zu's son) was used to set off Mi Heng, the Parrot Island Ode was used as Mi Heng's spiritual confession, and Huang Zu's impatience and the legal clerk's use of the opportunity to avenge personal grudges were used as the connecting thread of the event. The historical events were the main focus, and no distortion or explanation was added. Surprisingly, the new meaning could be clearly conveyed, and I believed that it conformed to the basic principles of historical essays.

Class Suspension

— Ren Daquan

Dragging his melancholy steps, Mr. Wang walked out of the principal's office, hands clasped behind his back, heading towards the school.

His heart felt strangely stifled, and his thick, dark eyebrows were tightly furrowed on his pale, thin face. His mind was empty, filled only with the smiling face of the principal, with his flat mouth opened wide, toothless. The words that came out of that flat mouth were still echoing in Mr. Wang's ears—

"Mr. Wang, alas! I'm really very sorry… Truly, brother, I'm very apologetic! Alas! … But, Mr. Wang, there's really no way! You think, the harvest is so bad, who in the village can afford to study? Alas! … If the harvest were good, it wouldn't be like this, alas! … Then we'll have to suspend classes temporarily, there's really nothing to be done without money, Mr. Wang, right? I personally certainly hope to maintain it, but the reality is this, there's no way! Alas! … No way! …"

Stepping over the school threshold, Mr. Wang released his hands from behind his back and sighed deeply.

As soon as they heard the teacher's voice, a large group of children playing together scattered with a "Ya!" and returned to their seats, eyes fixed on their books, pretending to be very attentive, mumbling sentences that they themselves couldn't hear clearly.

Normally, Mr. Wang would have frowned and scolded sternly: "Playing again, not studying hard, you won't be dismissed until you can recite your lessons!" Or he would stand in front of any child and point to the book, saying: "Read it clearly to me, read it word by word, what are you mumbling about?"

Today, Mr. Wang only glanced at each child's face and silently returned out of the school gate.

In front of the school gate was a large mulberry field with dense leaves, a sea of green as far as the eye could see.

Looking at the clusters of deep green mulberry leaves, Mr. Wang remembered when he first came to teach at this rural elementary school, the mulberry trees were just bare branches. It was truly unexpected! The school would close after only one semester. Although the life of a teacher was quite poor, guiding thirty or forty naughty children all day long, the souls of these barefoot, ragged children were pure and innocent. Their faces often had innocent and lovely smiles without a trace of pretense…

But it's over! Besides the sorrow of being unemployed, Mr. Wang's heart was also filled with a deep sense of loss.

A burst of sharp and energetic shouts from the children called Mr. Wang back into the room.

…………………

The next morning, the school was strangely lively: children who were usually lazy and late all came early, their little faces covered with a melancholic expression. Pairs of lively eyes stared blankly at the teacher, who was busy packing his luggage, and the teacher also stole glances at them from time to time.

"Will the teacher come back after leaving?"

"We haven't even read half a textbook in Chinese!"

"Why doesn't the teacher teach us anymore and want to go back? It's so good here."

"We don't want the teacher to leave, teacher, don't go!"

Listening to the soft and quiet questions, Mr. Wang smiled bitterly.

The principal and a porter carrying the luggage arrived. The porter picked up the luggage, and Mr. Wang followed closely behind, leaving the school gate. The principal and a large group of children followed, seeing him off to the road outside the village that led to the city.

"Mr. Wang, goodbye! Goodbye!" the principal said, opening his flat mouth.

"Ah! Principal, goodbye!"

"Teacher! Teacher!"

Mr. Wang turned his head and saw that the children's eyes were mostly wet and glistening.

The road was long, and Mr. Wang seemed to still hear a burst of strangely affectionate cries in his ears:

"Teacher! Teacher!"

Sound of Clothes Beating

Towards Evening (4)

— Qu Yi

"Chunyang Inn—Chunyang Inn, is it not?" The shorter one raised his head and smiled. At the same time, he also stopped. A girl and an old woman then passed through the pair standing there. The taller and shorter ones both turned their heads to look at the girl. A pale white face, two fiery red cheeks. The eyes were swollen and tired. Her entire figure revealed an immature injury.

Both forgot what they should say.

"A yes—going, ah!" Immediately a contrived voice floated up from the side. The old woman's face, like a pomelo rind, appeared before them.

"Hmph!" Each spat out a frivolous sound from his nose. Each felt that his eyes should take a bath to be clean. And so they immediately floated their eyes towards Zhongshan Road, wanting to find an ocean for eyes with smoke-like light!

"Is it not?" The shorter one then waved his short legs and walked off. At the same time, he took out a piece of paper from his pants pocket. "Opposite Dahan Company, Chunyang Inn, Room 13! Please come for a chat. Sincerely, Guo Ren, Brothers Li An, from your brother Hu Yiyuan." Looking at it, he read it out loud.

This time, the taller one followed the shorter one. But the taller one always felt as if a single step would kick through the shorter one's butt, and so he dared not take large strides.

Chunyang Inn was opposite Dahan Company. But Dahan Company's rooftop was higher than Chunyang Inn. Dahan Company's facade was also wider than Chunyang Inn. This naturally matched pair walked in front of Dahan Company, but still could not find Chunyang Inn. And so they stopped again on the sidewalk, stretching their heads to look at Dahan Company.

Shen Bao Local Supplement

Talks

Remarriage and Widow Marriage

— Xing An

The principle is very simple. Before national laws explicitly state otherwise, men who lose their wives can remarry, and women who lose their husbands can of course remarry as well. However, the situation in China is different. Chinese society only allows men who have lost their wives to remarry, but does not allow women who have lost their husbands to remarry. This is not a strange thing, because China is a land that values ​​ethics and morality the most! Of the three unfilial acts, having no descendants is the greatest. A man who has the responsibility of carrying on the family line, if his wife dies, and he does not remarry to have someone take her place, I ask, who will inherit the ancestral incense? It is best if he is willing to remarry. If there is a man who does not want to remarry after his wife dies, I am afraid that his relatives and clansmen will find a woman for him and force him to have children with her! As for women, starving to death is a small matter, losing chastity is a great matter. If a woman who loses her husband does not think of hanging herself to die in honor, she is already not considered a perfect heroine. Would she be allowed to remarry? Remarriage would not only disgrace the family, but would also shatter the existing morality! If someone asks me, why does Chinese society treat men and women so differently? I can only answer that this is how etiquette has always been. Is this answer not enough for you?

People like to take two recent events that happened in Chinese society and compare them, criticize them, and use them to attack the unreasonableness of the old etiquette. One is the wedding of Xiong and Mao, which shook Shanghai society and was praised as a good story. The other is the wedding of Wang and Wei, which shocked Tianjin society and became a joke. The reason why these two marriages were praised as a good story and became a joke is because the former was the remarriage of a man who had lost his wife, and the latter was the remarriage of a woman who had lost her husband. Otherwise, if they were just two ordinary marriages, they would not have attracted so much attention.

In fact, those who take these two marriages to compare and criticize are a bit far-fetched. Because the wedding of Xiong and Mao is one thing, and the wedding of Wang and Wei is another thing. These two things, from the point of view of men remarrying and women remarrying, the former is encouraged by the old morality, and the latter is prohibited by the old etiquette, so they cannot be compared. Moreover, the protagonist of the remarriage is a man with a special status in society, and the protagonist of the remarriage is a concubine of a man with a high status in society. Can you blame the social figures for praising the wedding of Xiong and Mao and ridiculing the wedding of Wang and Wei? Wei Wenxiu's denunciation and expulsion is exactly the guilt that a shameless and unchaste widow deserves! Now that she has fled to West Lake to knock on wooden fish amidst the siege of all sides, is it not too late to regret it? Gentlemen and guardians of morality cannot but be deeply saddened!

However, those who are fighting for injustice against the remarriage of Wei Wenxiu can at most bring out Chinese law as a talisman, saying that the law of the Republic of China does not have an explicit provision prohibiting widows from remarrying, so Wei's remarriage is actually allowed by national law. Moreover, Wei's combination with Li is only as a concubine, and remarriage is her own right and freedom, and is not bound by law. And marriage is a private act, so how can others intervene? But ah, those who are calling for justice for Wei, you must not forget that in addition to the tangible laws, there are also intangible morals. Wei's remarriage, even if allowed by law, cannot escape the sanctions of the old social morality. If a woman can remarry after her husband dies, how can the two words "chastity" be preserved? Moreover, Li Gong was once the president of the country!

I dare to make an arbitrary statement: in China, a male-dominated society can be maintained for at least another five hundred years!

Farewell

— Zhou Han

The spring rain was blowing softly, and although it was already dawn, the clouds were densely interwoven, as if it were still early. Yu Yu looked out the window for a moment, not wanting to get up. His wife didn't believe it was still early, so she turned on the light on the bedside table, looked at her watch, and exclaimed, "Oh my, it's already half past six!" Half past six, if she didn't get up, how would she make it in time? The two quickly dressed, washed their faces, and prepared their luggage. The suitcase and miscellaneous items had been packed the night before, and now they only had to tie up the bedding. Two quilts were to be taken, and in addition, a blanket was needed. "Okay, take them all," Yu Yu said, starting to pack the bedding. Not having experience, the first time he packed it, it was loose and big. The second time he packed it tighter, but it was still very big. So-so, there was no way, any later and they would miss the train. It was naturally troublesome for women to go out. Just the work of putting on makeup would take half an hour. He was packing the bedding while urging her to hurry, but makeup was a woman's only job, and she couldn't be careless about it. The more you urged her to hurry, the slower she became. The first time the powder was too thick, ugly, so she washed it off; the second time she felt it was too thin, so she added a little. The time she spent looking in the mirror was also especially long. She looked in the front, looked in the back, admiring herself in the mirror as if feeling sorry for herself, and that took up most of the time. Yu Yu finished packing the bedding, broke out in a sweat, and was already unhappy. Seeing her wasting valuable time like that, his temper flared up. If it were an ordinary outing, he would have already started scolding, but now she was going far away, and it was right to endure a little and let her feel his tenderness. Moreover, they had already quarreled the night before, so why leave her with a bad impression when she left? Thinking of this, Yu Yu remained silent and simply lit a cigarette to wait for her. And in the midst of the smoke, he recalled the scene of the quarrel last night.

His wife still didn't want to go home last night. Life was so poor, what reason was there not to go home? She couldn't say the reason. But she didn't want to go. Yu Yu lost his temper and said, "Okay, you don't want to go, fine. From now on, I'll take care of myself, you take care of yourself." His wife was stubborn and said defiantly, "You won't take care of me? Hmph, that's easier said than done! See, if I starve to death in Shanghai, it's not like you'll be any more glorious!" "Then you won't leave, what do you want me to do?" Yu Yu shouted loudly, and finally scolded, "Damn it, I owed you in my past life, and I'm paying it back in this life!" The reason why his wife didn't want to leave was just because the separation would be three years, she had only recently come to Shanghai to find him, and now she had to go back, she couldn't bear to separate emotionally—it was all about the emotion, but Yu Yu didn't care about that. He was completely a materialist, and had forgotten about emotions after being whipped by life. His wife understood that he didn't care about emotions, and couldn't help but feel sad and burst into tears. "I don't want to leave, I just don't want to leave you, but you scold me as if I'm worthless, what kind of person have you become?" She cried loudly, which made Yu Yu even more uncomfortable, and a feeling of sadness and hatred arose from his annoyance. "Tsk tsk tsk, women,..." Saying that, he realized that he was really too ruthless, and with a change of heart, he felt a little regretful, and his voice became gentle and peaceful. "It's not that I want you to leave me, but, you have to know, I've been unemployed for a long time, and life is impossible. It's already difficult for me to support myself in Shanghai, if I add another person, what can I do?" He went up to comfort her, saying some heartfelt words, and only then did his wife agree to leave.

Now it was already late, and his wife was still deliberately wasting time putting on makeup, wanting to lose his temper but feeling that he shouldn't, and not losing his temper was really unbearable. He took a few puffs of his cigarette and shouted at her, "So-so, okay,... hurry, hurry;" His wife saw his anxiety and irritability in the mirror, and felt both sad and amused in her heart. A thought also arose in her mind, to spend a little more time putting on makeup, to miss the train schedule; if she couldn't leave today, she would change it to tomorrow, if she couldn't leave tomorrow, she would change it to the day after tomorrow; to stay a few more days. But because they had already quarreled last night, staying would lead to a decisive break, so she dismissed the idea.

The two took a car to the North Station, and it was already late. The people seeing them off on the platform were already waiting by the train carriages. After Yu Yu settled his wife down, he only said one sentence, "Don't worry, I'll write to you and call you to come as soon as I can." His wife's eyes were red and moist. "The train is about to leave, I'm leaving." Saying that, he got off the train, without even turning his head, and went straight out of the platform.

A Helping Hand

— Yi An

Feelings of the Past and Present

— Mao Hua

What I am about to say are things that happened six or seven years ago. During my trips back to my hometown during the winter and summer vacations, I always saw many beggars coming to the door to beg; asking for rice, asking for leftover rice, asking for copper coins, as long as you were willing to give, they wanted everything. Moreover, they had ways of contacting each other. As long as one beggar got something at your house, he would immediately notify the other beggars when he left, making your courtyard like a marketplace, and you would be too busy to attend to them all.—That situation was very annoying to me!

At that time, I had received a little education, and I was extremely opposed to giving alms to beggars. I thought that a person should work, should engage in productive work, and should use physical strength to exchange for food. Beggars, on the other hand, are clearly consumers, not producers. Although there may be a few people who are excluded from the circle of life, and begging out of shame is forced upon them, it is excusable. But based on the saying "Begging for three years, lazy to be emperor", there are indeed many people who are content with a free and leisurely begging life and do not think of extricating themselves! Therefore, giving alms to them is exactly harming them, exactly increasing their laziness, and exactly burying their future.—This is the simple reason why I oppose giving alms.

But my mother's opinion was exactly the opposite of mine. She thought that it was always good to give alms, and when there was nothing to give alms, the family would be unlucky. Obviously, she had a superstitious idea, and part of the supporters of that idea was the old saying "Large donations lead to great wealth". She sincerely hoped that the family fortune would improve year by year!

I couldn't bear to go against my mother's heart, and after arguing a few sentences, I let her have her way.

However, the places where my mother and I disagreed were not limited to dealing with beggars. Like burning "New Year's Eve dinner" on New Year's Eve was also a subject of controversy. According to tradition, my mother always liked to burn a lot of New Year's Eve dinner, until the fifth day of the new year, "Road God's birthday", to stop. I was extremely disgusted with eating leftover rice every day. When my mother was hiding in the rice bin scooping rice, I always made a fuss about scooping less, so as not to eat leftover rice every day. But she didn't say anything, just ignored it.

I listened impatiently: she called a name and scooped a liter of rice. There were seventeen or eighteen people in the family, so she scooped seventeen or eighteen liters of rice. Moreover, some of them were children under the age of three, and actually my grandmother and great-grandmother who did not eat at my house, she also counted their food, didn't she scoop a few more liters of rice out of thin air? However, I didn't say anything anymore, anyway, she would ignore it.

Later on, I heard her say that the cat also gets a liter, and the dog also gets a liter, which made me have to explode. But her answer was very simple: "Cats have cat food, dogs have dog food". I knew that arguing would not be effective, so I had to stretch my throat and eat leftover rice.

Obviously, my mother's idea was again built on the hope of a good omen. She hoped to have enough food and clothing, and the family would improve year by year!

The development of the facts is terrible. That was already six or seven years ago, but compared with the situation today, the rapid decline of the family is really making us feel extremely terrified! Now, the fields are gone, and we eat grain all year round, which is very miserable and tragic. When beggars come to the door, we are reluctant to give alms anymore. In fact, there is nothing to give alms, and we often end up driving them away with harsh words, and the atmosphere is very bad!

Now, whether there is rice for New Year's Eve dinner is still a question: even if there is rice for New Year's Eve dinner, whether the creditors will let us eat it is still a question.—Because of many questions, my mother is constantly thinking in depression, seeking a solution; undoubtedly, her previous dream has been shattered, and the generous methods of "cats have cat food, dogs have dog food" when scooping rice can no longer be used. Moreover, even if I'm afraid of eating leftover rice, there's no need for me to object!

On the Way to Relief

— Chen Liang

Also unable to care about the whistling cold wind outside, and the heavy sky covered with red clouds, was progressing towards severity. Although the partners all felt a bit timid, showing a spider-like expression, the responsibility we bear is really too great. In another place, there are countless starving refugees, male, female, old, young... groaning, weeping, holding their shrunken bellies, stretching their thin necks, hoping for our group. Countless lives about to die, waiting urgently for us to rescue them, we are the people who give relief.

After eating breakfast hastily, we took the Yongche bus at nine o'clock to District Seven. We got off at the crossroads at eleven o'clock. The cold wind mercilessly tried its best to blow on us. The cotton robes fluttered up like single garments. Everyone had to grit their teeth, hug their chests tightly with both hands. After walking a few steps, snowflakes began to sprinkle on the ground. Someone was the first to shout: "What to do, it's snowing!"

"It's better to snow, it won't be very cold on a snowy day." I said, this was just a word to comfort people's hearts. After all, we were not sitting in a room with doors and windows closed. This place was still sixty miles away from our destination on a rugged mountain road. We didn't bring anything to keep out the cold. Several partners who were used to sitting in the office naturally couldn't help but complain. The wind in the mountains was like sharp steel arrows stabbing everyone's face from the fluttering snowflakes. The snowflakes rested on the eyelashes and melted into water droplets. The hands hiding in the pockets did not dare to reach out to wipe them.

In the hearts of several weaker partners, they were preparing not to move forward. I had to advise them again: "Please endure some more hardship, countless dying lives are in our hands!"

Looking up at the sky, hot air flowed out of the mouth and disappeared into the wind and snow.

"The snow will probably stop, right? Look at the sky over there, it's very bright..." But the snowballs in front of us were getting bigger and bigger, and denser and denser. The front had become a blurred wilderness, and it was almost impossible to tell the way. There was no way to think. With great difficulty, we found a few sedan chairs in a village. We agreed to pay 1.5 yuan per sedan to carry us forty miles to the foot of the mountain. However, halfway there, the porters with bare legs and feet could not bear the cold, and at the same time, they were afraid of not being able to find their way back after dark. They voluntarily took half of their money and asked us to get off and continue on our way by ourselves. There was no way to force them, so we had to grit our teeth and run again, run again...

The turtle-shaped stone slab road was covered with snow, and coupled with the stiff legs that had been sitting in the sedan chair for twenty miles, we were slipping and falling from time to time. And the wind was still so strong, and the snow was still so heavy. The partners started to complain again, "We are going to give relief to the disaster victims, but now we ourselves are suffering the same hardships as the disaster victims. We are still being told that we are eating off the disaster victims, damn it! This is so infuriating. The gentlemen and ladies with charity titles at most spend some money to watch a voluntary play or participate in a disaster relief art exhibition..." A never-ending series.

"Forget it, "die when the goods reach the snake's head", you have to go now, you have to go even if you don't want to!"

Simply take off the hat, loosen the clothes, climb the mountain... The guide finally said a word to reassure people: "The Shangkengtang place in District Seven where you are staying for the night is about to arrive."

A vast expanse of white sky, a vast expanse of white earth. The time was six o'clock, and there was still some light in the sky. After passing the fourth mountain frog, a Mr. Ma really came down the mountain to pick us up. The partners all shook off the snow on their shoulders at the same time, and their feet also felt warm.

Felling Teak

— Jing Yun

In the early morning, the orange-red sunlight filtered through the lush green teak leaves, leaving patches of golden, shimmering sunlight on the ground.

Beautiful little birds, full of life, hopped on the branches, facing the orange-red sun, singing "Good Morning" songs. Looking out from the gaps in the branches and leaves, the clear and bright blue sky was filled with light, floating white clouds.

An endless forest, like a vast blue-green sea, was surrounded by milky-white morning mist. The mist wandered through the forest, light and thin, like smoke rising from the thatched roofs of the natives, or like the light curtains on the windows of Westerners.

In the forest, besides the simple music produced by saws on the teak trees, the air was as quiet as a lonely ancient temple standing in the deep mountains.

A gust of morning wind came down from the canopy-like teak treetops, rustling and swirling around the elderly He Xingbo, who was working below pulling a saw, making him shiver repeatedly, his body covered in goosebumps.

"After all, I'm getting old, old people are really useless, I can't even stand this little morning breeze." He Xingbo stopped his work and sighed unintentionally, while buttoning up the buttons on his chest. "At this time, Wanggu is hot and stuffy, but here—Bayap (Bayap is in northern Siam, more than 500 miles from Wanggu.)—the weather is already like the late autumn season." He then struck up a conversation with the local working next to him.

"He Xingbo, why don't you return to 'Tangshan'? Do you want to spend your whole life in Siam?" The "native," whose face was as black as charcoal, seemed to be concerned about the elderly He Xingbo, who had left his hometown and was living a wandering life in a "foreign land." "Isn't that right? After a hundred years, a person's bones must return to their 'homeland' to be at peace!" He then took out a prepared "betel quid" from his pocket, added a piece of betel nut, and chewed it with great relish.

"Return to 'Tangshan,'... 'Tangshan,' I have nothing!"

This clearly stirred up a long-forgotten matter in He Xingbo's heart, causing it to resurface. He repeated, saying: a worm of melancholy suddenly crawled onto his face, which was covered with a layer like dried bean curd skin.

"What? Isn't there a son in your home in Tangshan?"

"He died early!"

"Then, what about a daughter-in-law?"

"How can a poor family keep a young woman? Before her husband had even been dead for a hundred days, she went off with someone else!..." He Xingbo's face became even more melancholy and ugly, gloomy like the sky on a rainy day.

"Tui," the native spat out a mouthful of blood-like saliva, then pulled out two Silver Root Hidemeng brand cigarettes from his pocket, struck a match, and handed one to He Xingbo. Then, wisps of mist-like white smoke leisurely puffed out of their mouths.

Rustling, the teak trees again played simple music under the saw, but in He Xingbo's heart, he was filled with sorrow, softly lamenting his uncertain fate, like the teak being taken away from the forest, drifting everywhere. ...…

Shen Bao Local Supplement - Film Special

The Exciting Revolution of 1935: "Color Films" Will Replace Sound Films

— Zhu Jiabo

1935 may be another memorable revolutionary milestone in the history of world cinema!

In any case, Hollywood has made considerable preparations and is quietly awaiting the outbreak of this revolution. The last major revolution in the film industry was seven years ago. At that time, "The Jazz Singer" suddenly turned Hollywood's film industry into sound films, making silent films relics of the past. Major film companies had to quickly raise an extra 100 million yuan in capital to engage in the production of sound films. At that time, the Hollywood film industry was fundamentally shaken, causing all producers, film merchants, directors, stars, etc., to lose color in their faces.

Now 1935 is already among us. Hollywood, or perhaps not just Hollywood, is once again in a state of panic. They know that the changes of the times are inevitable, and the revolutionary tide is irreversible. But this change affects the entire film industry, how can they not reminisce about the past and talk about tigers?

However, the last time it was sound films that revolutionized silent films. What will revolutionize sound films this time? Not Television or broadcast movies. That period still needs to wait a few more years. The hero rising now is color films!

Now the people in Hollywood, no matter who they are, no matter where they are, they start and end their conversations with color. What two-component color, what three-component color, can be heard everywhere, making outsiders feel that the people in Hollywood are all in a frenzy. In fact, how can they not be afraid? Isn't this a phenomenon of "the mountain rain is coming, and the wind fills the tower"?

Some people say that the upcoming era of color films may be even greater than the era of sound films we have already seen. Why? Sound films are certainly a major change and a major advancement, but, taking the world as a whole, we must know that only 65 percent of the world's cinemas have sound film projection equipment. However, when color films come out, all cinemas can be without the need to add special equipment. Wouldn't the future color films be more popular than the current sound films?

In fact, in the past year, 1934, and the beginning of this year, we have already seen a part of the face of this emerging color film. That is the scene of the final audience with the British court in George Arliss' "The House of Rothschild," and the scene of the large ice cream bucket in Eddie Cantor's "Kid Millions." The beauty and harmony of the colors we saw in these two scenes were far beyond our expectations. Because this color photography technique is the "three-component color" photography technique mentioned above. Prior to this, what we saw was only "two-component color," which only had red and green colors. In the "two-component color" photography technique, only two colors are available, so the result is extremely unsatisfactory, and everything except large red and large green colors is dim and dull. Now, after the invention of the "three-component color" photography technique, the color distribution is extremely harmonious, and the color range is much wider.

In this era of improvement, we cannot fail to mention the names of two great men. One is the inventor of "three-component color," Dr. Herbert T. Kalmus, and the other is the creator of Mickey Mouse, Walt Disney. As early as more than 20 years ago, in 1914, Kalmus gathered many like-minded people and organized a research institute to specifically explore methods of color projection on the screen. They were all graduates of the Massachusetts Institute of Technology. They later invented a color photography method and adopted their alma mater's nickname (Tech), calling the newly invented color photography technique Technicolor.

Progress is very slow. But in 1921, they used "Technicolor" to make a film for the first time. Of course, from a commercial standpoint, it didn't achieve any success. But they still moved forward relentlessly, and many color and photography experts in the United States also helped them wholeheartedly, making them even more inspired and energetic. After sound films became popular in 1927, they felt the necessity of color in films even more. It is true that there are several song and dance films that have added color interludes, which increased the audience's interest a lot.

In the recent five or six years, the application of Technicolor has stagnated, and the revolution of color films has been hindered until now. The reason is that there were not many cameras that could shoot color films to meet the needs of the film industry. There were also not many technical talents available for the employment of various companies. But during this period, Kalmus and his team achieved amazing success in their research! That is, they advanced from the two-component color of red and green to the three-component color of red, yellow, and blue.

Walt Disney's contribution is also very considerable. After Kalmus' experiment was successful, and all the filmmakers were hesitating due to their disappointment with the previous two-component color, he resolutely signed a one-year patent contract with Kalmus. Walt Disney wanted to make a full-color feature film in these few months. He said: "I don't want to turn Mickey Mouse or the Silly Symphonies into color films. I want to go one step further and make a full-length comedy film, using color to shoot it."

Okay, let's watch. Let us quietly await the arrival of this brand-new era of color films!

Hollywood Figures' Impressions of China

— Yimin

Historically, the United States has viewed China as an extremely uncivilized country, where men still wear queues and women still bind their feet. They believe that Chinatown is the only representative place in China. Therefore, almost all films depicting the social conditions of China have disgusting ugliness.

People in Hollywood are also not aware of the state of China. Because of the decline of China's international status, they have developed a contemptuous mentality. However, in recent years, there are more and more Hollywood people who understand China. They came to China to visit with curiosity and returned with a very good impression. The following are these people's impressions of China:

Liliana Damita once visited Beiping, China. She has a very detailed study of Beiping's people and customs. She often said to people: "Beiping, China, is indeed a famous city in world history. I have been to the old palace. I believe that China is indeed an advancing country. The people of Beiping are all kind and friendly. The clerks in the shops are like German merchants, friendly and polite. I only stayed in Beiping for more than three months, which made me extremely reluctant to leave. The scenery of Beiping is even better. There are many places that Hollywood doesn't have. Even now, I still miss that ancient city with its simple and honest customs."

Laura La Plante has an even deeper impression of China. She grew up in Hong Kong. She lived in various places in Guangdong. She can speak fluent Cantonese. She has worked as a stage actress in Guangdong. She knows the social conditions of China very well. Her view is: "China has its own unique human relationships and customs. The old morality of the Chinese people is very strict. The Chinese people attach great importance to politeness. Although general education is not universal in China, the people of the lower classes also have very good etiquette. The other thing is credit. Chinese merchants often do not sign any contracts or agreements when doing business with each other. They have a word for it, and at that time they will definitely deliver the goods and pay the money, with very few unexpected disputes."

William Powell has the following views on China: "I have been to the north and south of China. My view on Guangdong is that it is the most civilized place in China. The people in Guangdong have a spirit of adventure, which is a unique characteristic and is not as good as people in other provinces. Shanghai is just an important place for cultural and material transportation. It is also the most prosperous place in the East. Even China's film industry is mostly concentrated here. Beiping and Tianjin are both very good places that retain China's unique customs. The loyalty of the people and the simplicity of the customs have their own beauty. When I arrived in Beiping, I hoped that China's film city would be in Beiping, and the Hollywood of the East might be in Beiping."
