Moscow to Build a 20,000-Seat Grand Theater

Moscow, the capital of Soviet Russia, is currently constructing the world's largest cinema. The cinema is being built in the "Entertainment" park, covering an area of two acres. Once completed, it will be able to accommodate 20,000 spectators. The theater is also planning to install a 500-square-foot screen and purchase projection and sound equipment with a million candlepower from abroad, as Soviet Russia is not yet able to manufacture such powerful equipment itself. All thirty major theaters in Moscow are usually full, so seats must be reserved several hours before each show, and for popular films, reservations must be made a day in advance. Recently, the most distinctive films shown have been "Tchabaeff" and "Gay Fellow." "Tchabaeff" is a historical film depicting Russian military heroes. "Gay Fellow," on the other hand, is purely a comedy without any propaganda content. Both films are comparable to "The Thief of Bagdad," starring Douglas Fairbanks, which broke audience records several years ago. Few British and American films are shown in Moscow, and those that are are mostly old films.

Movie Novel

National Call (Bordertown) (7)

— Xue

After a sudden change in her body and face, Marie Roark suddenly screamed, "You—if it weren't for me, you'd still be a waiter at the Silver Shoe. I made you rich! The clothes you wear, I gave them to you. Now—you just washed your neck and think you're a high-class person. No one can do that—you're born a lowly thing—just like me. You belong to me—don't even think about leaving me!" Johnny clenched his teeth and slowly said, "No, I can't be with you. I know what kind of person I want. You can't control me. I'm going up." Marie shouted, "What right does she have over you? You belong to me. I'll never let go! I committed murder for you!"

Johnny asked strangely, "What? What crime did you commit?" Marie said, "I killed him—I killed him. It was for you." Johnny, looking dismissive, slowly said, "Looking at you gives me a headache. From now on, be careful, know what's good for you, stay far away from this place, far away from me." After he finished speaking, he went out to look for Dale Elwell, but the moonlight still shone brightly in the greenhouse, and his sweetheart was nowhere to be found.

Perhaps Dale didn't think about meeting him again. Perhaps in Dale's heart, there was no trace of Johnny Ramirez. Indeed, the next day when Johnny went to the Elwell residence to visit her, Elwell's butler tried to stop him, but the current Johnny was not someone the butler could stop. When he went inside and met Dale, Dale couldn't help but laugh. She readily agreed to go for a ride with him in his new car. In his straightforward and love-struck eyes, what other explanation could there be for her behavior?

One afternoon, Johnny happily walked into his office. He saw Marie sitting on his desk. Johnny frowned and said, "Didn't I tell you to come here less?" Marie smiled and said, "Is the great lover so busy that no one is here to take care of things?" Johnny said, "Okay, please take care of things more often from now on. I'm going back to the old place." Marie controlled herself and said with a smile, "Oh, so you've already discussed it with that woman. You must be very happy, right?" Johnny casually said, "Yeah, couldn't be happier. After I sign the checks and pay the salaries, I'm going back to the old place to open an even bigger one. She invited me to go out and play for a few days. When we come back, we're going to get engaged."

As Johnny spoke, his back was to Marie, so he didn't see the change in Marie's face, the burning anger in her heart, which made her face look terribly strange. He only heard Marie say, "Since things have come to this, I can only let you go... but I wish you a happy future." As she spoke, she reached out her hand. Johnny didn't understand what she meant, but he couldn't辜負 her kindness, so he also reached out his hand and shook hers. Marie continued, "I'm saying this from the bottom of my heart. I'd rather see you rise step by step. I'd rather see you have endless happiness."

These words gradually made him feel uneasy. He let go of her hand and said, "I have a lot of things to do. I need to hurry. I need to pack Golf's clothes and the tuxedo... See you later." Marie said kindly, "Okay, Johnny, see you later." The smile on her face remained until Johnny went out. However, as soon as the door closed, her face changed again. She muttered to herself, "... He told me to kill him—Johnny Ramirez—he said if I didn't do it, he would beat me to death—I was afraid of him—I had to do it—Johnny wanted the money—he knew that when he died, the money would be in his hands—" Will this plan succeed? Her cunning mind pondered. (To be continued)
